Discharged Employees of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Petition for Reinstatement Yesterday

Central News Agency: The Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is actively laying off redundant employees to reduce expenses due to financial difficulties. On the 16th of this month, it ordered the layoff of 101 employees from the five warehouses. The discharged employees were all indignant at the sudden dismissal by the Bureau and organized a petitioning group to repeatedly request the Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to explain the reasons for the layoff and demand reinstatement of all employees, but to no avail. Furthermore, opinions among the employees were divided, so they did not formally submit a letter explaining the reasons. Yesterday afternoon, about 30 of the discharged employees gathered at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, seeking to see the directors, but yesterday was Saturday afternoon, and the Bureau was not working. Furthermore, none of the directors were responsible. The employees waited for a long time and did not see any directors arrive at the Bureau. They then called all the executive directors, but none of them were at home. They had no choice but to disperse around 5:00 PM, declaring that they would go to the Bureau again next Monday to sit and wait, and would bring bedding and food to stay at the Bureau. While the employees were waiting at the Bureau, they complained incessantly. In summary, there were three reasons: (1) The central government ordered industrial institutions throughout the country to accommodate as many unemployed people as possible in order to stabilize society; (2) The Three Principles of the People of the Premier are based on the people's livelihood, but the Bureau's severance of the livelihoods of the majority of small employees violates the posthumous instructions; (3) The Bureau does not actively seek to expand and increase operations, but rather uses financial difficulties to increase social unrest, which is inconsistent with the central government's principle of resisting foreign aggression and securing domestic stability. Some radical individuals even declared that they would organize a hunger strike to show their determination.

Director of the Maritime Bureau, Zhu Yaoting, Assumed Office Yesterday

The Ministry of Transportation Appointed Wan Huiyi as Supervisor

Chen Yici and Yu Shifan Appointed as Section Chiefs

He Hanlan, Director of the Shanghai Maritime Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation, had previously submitted his resignation. Zhu Yaoting, the First Section Chief of the Zhejiang Construction Department, was appointed by the Ministry to succeed him. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday to take over. The handover is detailed below:

Handover Ceremony: The new Director of the Shanghai Maritime Bureau, Zhu Yaoting, arrived in Shanghai to discuss handover procedures with He Hanlan after receiving the Ministry's order, and set the 21st as the date to take office. Director He had already instructed all sections to prepare for the handover. Yesterday morning at around 9:00 a.m., Zhu Yaoting, accompanied by Chen Yici, Yu Shiying, and Wan Yaoyi, the supervisor from the Ministry of Transportation, arrived at the Maritime Bureau at No. 6 Sichuan Road. Former Director He welcomed them in. After a brief rest, they were led into a temporary hall in the reception room. Director He first gathered all the staff from the first and second sections, and after the formalities, Director He began by stating that since taking office, he had started to organize maritime affairs and was beginning to see progress. He regretted that the time was too short to achieve his goals. He said that in his past work, he had done his best to fulfill his duties with integrity. After his speech, new Director Zhu Yaoting held the inauguration ceremony. Former Director He handed over the seals, documents, and public funds to the new director and then withdrew.

Director's Address: After taking office, new Director Zhu Yaoting issued an address. He first stated that former Director He was a specialist in maritime affairs, and the Shanghai Maritime Bureau had achieved obvious results under his leadership, which were worthy of emulation. He himself had served as the First Section Chief and concurrently as a technical expert in the Zhejiang Construction Department, and had also managed the provincial ship office in Zhejiang Province. Although the scope was smaller, the nature was the same. He said that he was deeply willing to follow the norms set by Director He, continue to work hard on reform, and make the maritime administration achieve the hope of rejuvenation. He said that all those in the bureau who were familiar with the situation of their duties were people he still needed to rely on, and he ordered them to continue to serve with peace of mind.

Committee Member's Supervision: The Ministry of Transportation specially appointed Wan Huiyi, Section Chief of the Maritime Affairs Department, to come to Shanghai to supervise the handover from Director He to the new Director Zhu, and to represent the Minister in administering the oath-taking ceremony for Director Zhu. After the handover was completed, Wan delivered an address, expressing his hope that maritime affairs would be reformed and gradually achieve the recovery of maritime rights.

Appointment of Section Chiefs: The Maritime Bureau's organization is divided into only two sections. The original First Section Chief, Lu Esheng, and the Second Section Chief, Wu Daming, also submitted their resignations after He Hanlan resigned. Yesterday, the new Director approved them and immediately announced the appointments of Chen Yici as the First Section Chief and Yu Shifan as the Second Section Chief. Yu Shiying was appointed as Secretary. Chen Yici sent staff to take over the accounting and general affairs sections first, while Yu Shifan took over the technical section. At 12:00, the telegrams of He Hanlan's resignation and Director Zhu's inauguration were sent to the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing.

Public Announcement: The Maritime Bureau issued its first public notice yesterday, stating, "It is hereby announced that the Ministry of Transportation's Order No. 587 states: 'He Hanlan, Director of the Shanghai Maritime Bureau, is to be appointed to another position. Zhu Yaoting is appointed to fill the vacancy. In addition to separate orders, the relevant personnel are hereby ordered to comply with the order to take office, and to report the date of taking office and the handover situation.' Having received this order, we have taken office on January 22. In addition to reporting and distributing this notice, it is hereby announced to merchants and people to be informed."

Zhu's Brief Biography: Zhu, whose courtesy name is Youliao, is 39 years old, from Haiyan, Zhejiang. He graduated from Beiyang University and then went to Cornell University in the United States, where he obtained a Master's degree in Civil Engineering. He has served as an engineer for the New York State Department of Transportation, a construction engineer for the New York Central Railroad Company. After returning to China in the 12th year of the Republic, he served as a professor at Hehai University, Director of the Public Works Bureau of the Hangzhou Municipal Government, Director of the Engineering Department of the West Lake Exposition, Senior Technical Expert of the Central Construction Commission, and Technical Expert of the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department, concurrently serving as the First Section Chief.

Dr. Lowe, Agricultural Advisor to the Ministry of Industries, Submits a Memorial to Minister Chen

Major Plan to Develop Chinese Agriculture

The Continental News reports that Dr. Lowe, Agricultural Advisor to the Ministry of Industries, has drafted a major plan to develop Chinese agriculture, which was submitted to Minister Chen Gongbo several weeks ago. Dr. Lowe believes that China urgently needs a major plan to develop agriculture. It is estimated that the nation spends no less than 600 million yuan annually on imports of cotton, rice, wheat, flour, etc., plus 300 million yuan on imported cotton textiles, totaling approximately 900 million yuan annually. If a comprehensive plan for agricultural development can be implemented quickly within the limits of talent and financial resources, then these goods would no longer need to be imported, and this 900 million yuan could remain in the country. Dr. Lowe's plan covers all agricultural issues in detail. For the sake of administrative economy, all plans are summarized into four major groups: agricultural production, animal husbandry, agricultural economics and marketing, and agricultural experiment institutions. All work in these four groups is devoted to research, promotion, and inspection, with particular emphasis on research and experimentation, and the results are provided to farmers through promotional agencies. Under the agricultural production item, work is divided into crops, vegetables and fruits, forestry, soil science, tree diseases, and entomology. Under animal husbandry, it is divided into sericulture, poultry surveys, pig surveys, other livestock surveys, fisheries, animal diseases, and entomology, with special attention to sericulture. Under agricultural economics and marketing, there are farm management techniques, marketing, rural finance, general agricultural issues, rural institutions, and harvest reports. Regarding agricultural experiment institutions, it is advocated that the national government establish a central agricultural experiment station and establish provincial experiment stations in each province, which would be supervised by the central experiment station. The purpose of establishing the central agricultural experiment station is to investigate and organize national agricultural research and experimentation, and to provide appropriate supervision in terms of planning and work, in order to avoid duplication and save unnecessary waste. Although its planning covers all important national agricultural technologies, it is divided into categories, and each category is further divided into detailed items. A portion can be undertaken first within the scope of talent and financial resources, but this plan must be adopted in its entirety in order to achieve the effect of linkage and mutual assistance.

Regulations of the Chinese Aeronautical Association Submitted to the National Government Yesterday for Record

After being revised and passed by the second board of directors meeting, the regulations of the Chinese Aeronautical Association were submitted to the National Government for record yesterday. According to Lin Wojiang, the standing director of the Association, the full text of the regulations consists of six chapters and twenty-one articles, and the full text can be printed and distributed within about one propaganda week. The main points are extracted as follows:

Organization: Chapter 1 stipulates that a general association is to be established in Shanghai, an office in the capital, branch associations in various provinces and cities and overseas ports, and sub-associations in various counties and cities. Articles 8 to 15 of Chapter 3 stipulate that there will be twenty-one directors. The first session will be appointed by the National Government for a term of one year, and the second session will be elected by the members' representative assembly for a term of two years. The members' representative assembly will be held once a year, and the board of directors and the standing board of directors will each be held once a month. Under the board of directors, there will be five groups: general affairs, finance, design, organization, and propaganda. A fund management committee will also be established to show seriousness.

Members: Chapters 2 and 5 cover membership and fees. It is stipulated that any citizen of the Republic of China can join with the introduction of two or more members. There are two types of members: individual members and group members. Individual members are further divided into four types: ordinary members (paying two yuan per year), special members (paying ten yuan per year), supporting members (paying fifty yuan per year), and permanent members (paying five hundred yuan or more per year). Group members must pay sixty yuan or more per year.

Nisshin's Yangtze River Shipping Cannot Be Restored

Xiangyang Maru's Resumption of Navigation Again Hit by the Yu Guan Incident

Since Japanese goods have been implementing a dumping policy in the Yangtze River area of our country, the business of Nisshin Steamship Company's Yangtze River class has gradually improved, and Xiangyang Maru has resumed sailing. Recently, due to the Yu Guan incident, it has suffered a major blow. The details are as follows:

Resumption of Xiangyang: After the September 18th Incident, the business of Nisshin Steamship Company, which mainly operated the Yangtze River class, was affected by the interference of the people of our country, and the ships stopped sailing one after another. The Osaka headquarters repeatedly tried to reduce water freight and lower ticket prices, and used Chinese people to attract customers, exhausting all efforts, but to no avail. Only three ships on the Shanghai-Hankou class, Luoyang, Fengyang, and Nanyang, two ships on the Nanyang class, Songshan and Lushan, two ships on the Beiyang class, Tangshan and Huashan, one ship on the Hankou-Yichang class, and one ship on the Hankou-Changsha class, were barely sailing. The two classes from Yichang to Chongqing and from Changzhou to Changde were completely suspended. Since Japanese goods have been dumped in the Yangtze River area of ​​our country, the business of Nisshin's Yangtze River class has gradually improved. In December of last year, Xiangyang Maru was first resumed.

Again Affected: Since the resumption of Xiangyang Maru, there have been a total of four ships in the Yangtze River class. Most of the business is Japanese transshipment goods. The number of Chinese passengers has gradually increased after the price reduction. The company is preparing to resume Yueyang Maru and others. However, the Yu Guan incident has occurred again. Various business groups in our country have all notified the implementation of the initial intention to resist goods, resulting in a major blow to business and a sharp decline. The four ships that have been barely maintaining sailing on the Yangtze River class in recent days have had few Chinese people on each trip, all of whom are ignorant coolies. Chinese goods have disappeared, and Japanese transshipment goods have also decreased greatly compared with before. The Shanghai branch has telegraphed the headquarters and is trying to remedy the situation.

Department of Finance Sends Personnel to Supervise and Urge Road Construction Mu Tax

The Shanghai County Government and the Department of Finance ordered that the amount of road construction mu tax that should be remitted to the province by each county should be cleared on a monthly basis according to the regulations. However, many counties have been fatigued. Now, due to the urgent need for funds for the construction of provincial roads, in addition to sending Yu Xinmin to the county to supervise and urge the payment, the county is hereby ordered to prepare the amount of road construction mu tax that should be remitted in accordance with the plan and not delay it again.

Public Works Department Plans to Hold a Special Meeting of Taxpayers

To Discuss the Issue of Factory Licensing

In order to manage and inspect factories within the concession, the Public Works Department resolved on December 9, 1931, to find a way to convene a special meeting of taxpayers (foreigners) in order to pass the amendment to Section 34 of the Land Regulations (this section stipulates the businesses that should be licensed, and there is no word "factory" in the text). So that the Public Works Department has the power to deal with this matter. Later, due to the situation, it was decided in March of last year to postpone this matter. At the board of directors meeting on January 18 of this year, President Fessenden raised this matter again and stated the agreement he had reached with the former Chairman of the Board and the Chinese authorities on this matter last year. He also said that the Public Works Department had previously decided to invite Miss E.M. Hinder to the bureau to handle matters related to industrial affairs. Miss Hinder has now arrived at the bureau this month and has taken office. She suggested that a special meeting should be held on the day of this year's annual meeting (April 19) to implement the amendment to the attached law. Later, Chairman Bell said that the Carlton Theatre, where the annual meeting was held last time, was not large enough to accommodate the statutory number of people for a special meeting (according to a special meeting, one-third of the taxpayers must attend, that is, about a thousand people). If the new site of the Grand Theatre cannot be used at that time, only the Merchant Corps Parade Ground can be used. This matter needs to be investigated and reported by the Director of Public Works. The board of directors then decided to hold a special meeting of taxpayers on April 19 of this year in order to amend Section 34 of the attached law. If there are other matters that should be resolved at the special meeting, they will also be raised at that time. The text of the amendment will be drafted by the President.

Baihe River Ice Breaks, National Ships Stop Sailing to North China

National Ships Do Not Open to Tianjin: In recent days, the weather has been cold, and the Baihe River in Tianjin has been frozen for a long time. However, in the beginning, icebreakers could be used to guide navigation. Since the 17th of this month, the ice within Tanggu has been more than a foot thick, and the Baihe waterway has been completely frozen. After the Xinyuan ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was blocked by ice, it was the last ship to leave Tianjin. This return to Shanghai will stop sailing to North China. It has been notified to the Tianjin customer service to stop collecting passengers and goods to Tianjin. The ship will be diverted to Fuzhou. The Beiyang ships of other companies will also stop sailing to Jin and Gu from today.

Foreign Merchants Increase Freight Rates: During the time when Baihe River is frozen and Chinese ships stop sailing, the North American class ships of British merchants Taikoo and Jardine Matheson in this port are still dispatching ships. Shanghai has a large number of flour to be transported to Tianjin. Taikoo and Jardine Matheson are still loading them, but after arriving at Tanggu, they will find a way to transport them. The water freight will be increased by a quarter, from 1.2 yuan to 1.6 yuan per ton. Other goods will also be charged additional ice river water freight.

Japanese Ships Change to Dalian: The Tianjin class ships of Dalian Steamship Company, a Japanese merchant in this port, have been fixed to leave Tianjin on the 26th of this month. Due to the closure of the port of Baihe, they will no longer go to Tianjin and will temporarily change to Dalian. A notice has been issued yesterday.

Verdict on the Kidnapping Case of the Owner of Taichang Store: Three Kidnappers Sentenced to Death

＝The remaining eight criminals are sentenced to imprisonment for various terms＝

＝Lu Wanlin and two others declared innocent＝

Le Baozhen, the owner of Taichang Wood Store on Nanjing Road, was kidnapped by bandits on Yuyuan Road, and a huge ransom was demanded. Later, You A'gen, the chief Chinese detective of the Old Zhabei Police Station, Detective Liu Junqing, and Detective Chen Yonggui rescued Le from a bomb shelter at 911 Haig Road, and arrested 14 kidnappers, including Ma Gengsheng, Hu Hongsheng, Guan Afu, Cao Ziqing, Wang Xiaosizi, Li Youren, Cao Ziyu, Pan Yaoming, Zhang Jindizi, Ren Zixiang, Lu Gaolin, Zhou Jinsheng, Jin Zipei, and a woman named Chen Xushi. Three Mauser pistols, two handguns, a gas pistol, 253 bullets, and a car were seized. It was found that Ma and others had also kidnapped Yang Renshi, the young wife of Sheng Yishao, and demanded a ransom in two cases. They were handed over to the First Special Court for trial. Lu Wanlin hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to defend him. After interrogation and a final hearing, and after the four houses at 911 Haig Road, 139 Ma'saidillo Road, 39 Gaofu Lane, Saint Mary's Road, and 13 Yuhua Lane, Huishan Road were sealed, the verdict was pronounced yesterday morning. Zhan Jifeng, the lawyer for Lu Wanlin, and Ru Baoyi, the lawyer for the police station, were present on time to hear the verdict. At 9:00 a.m., Qian Changhongye, the head of the criminal division of the Special Court, ascended to the criminal court and announced the verdict. Except for Lu Wanlin, Chen Xushi, and Zhang Jindizi, who were declared innocent, the others were sentenced separately. Ma Gengsheng, Guan Afu, and Ren Zixiang were each sentenced to death, and deprived of their civil rights indefinitely. Jin Zipei, Cao Ziqing, and Wang Xiaosizi were each sentenced to life imprisonment, and deprived of their civil rights indefinitely. Hu Hongsheng was sentenced to 20 years of imprisonment, and deprived of his civil rights indefinitely. Li Youren and Zhou Jinsheng were each sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment, and deprived of their civil rights for 15 years. Cao Ziyu and Pan Yaoming were each sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. Three Mauser pistols, two handguns, a gas pistol, 253 bullets, and a car were confiscated. The items seized at 911 Haig Road, 139 Ma'saidillo Road, 39 Gaofu Lane, Saint Mary's Road, and 13 Yuhua Lane, Huishan Road, with the exception of the items at 139 Ma'saidillo Road, which Fan Hongshi and Du Fanshi are now claiming, and the items at 13 Yuhua Lane, which Lu Wanlin's lawyer Zhan claimed belonged to Lu's father and should be investigated and verified by the police station, will all be temporarily kept by the police station. If it is inconvenient to keep them, the original items will be auctioned off, and the proceeds will be sent to the court for safekeeping and collection.

Passengers Openly Kidnapped Next to the Train Station

Thieves Use Rental Cars

Cash Stolen from Victim

Zhao Jijing, a teacher at Datong University, arrived in Shanghai by train from Wuxi on the 5th of this month. When he exited the station, a rental car parked inside the station solicited business from Zhao, asking for one dollar for transportation to the school. Zhao found it very cheap and hired the car. Unexpectedly, the car was parked at the station by kidnappers specifically to kidnap foreign passengers. Zhao was kidnapped and hidden in a rural hut. The bandits originally planned to kidnap a wealthy merchant from Wuxi, but after repeatedly questioning Zhao, they realized they had kidnapped the wrong person and released him. However, more than 400 dollars in cash were stolen from Zhao, and when he was released, he was blindfolded with a pair of sunglasses and ordered to go to a desolate place and not to look, otherwise they would shoot. Therefore, Zhao was unable to identify the bandits' lair. After this case occurred, the Public Concession police severely cracked down on this type of kidnapper and sent a letter to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for assistance. Director Wen approved the letter, stating that the kidnappers parked cars in public transportation venues to kidnap passengers. It is said that he has ordered the detective team to step up the investigation.

Blind Woman Encounters a Villain

＝Greed Leads to Attempted Murder＝

＝Kidnapping and Theft Ultimately Exposed＝

Zhang Li, a blind woman from Nanshi, had some savings from her late husband. After her husband's death, she cohabitated with Zhang Ziliang. However, Zhang only lived with her for her money. After years of squandering, Zhang had used up several hundred yuan. He also kidnapped and sold her ten-year-old adopted daughter, Lan Ying. Zhang Li then negotiated with Zhang Ziliang, who asked his friend Li Darong to mediate with her, saying that Zhang would use 300 yuan to resolve the matter. Zhang Li immediately agreed and moved to Jin Bao's house on Sanguantang Road, Xieqiao, to await the resolution. Unexpectedly, on the 3rd of this month, Li Darong took her to collect the money, and pushed her into the Huangpu River in Yangshupu, intending to kill her, and then fled. After Zhang Li fell into the river, she was fortunately rescued by a boatman, but her forehead was broken. She reported to the police station and was sent to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. When she returned home the day before yesterday, all the belongings in her house and her five-year-old daughter, Zhang Linbao, had been kidnapped by Li Darong. Zhang Li cried and asked Ma Wu to go with her to the Second District to file a complaint. Fortunately, the detectives captured Li, who confessed that he had sold the child to Chen Dengshi's house in Xiaoshadu. Detectives were immediately sent to bring Chen Dengshi and the child together. The group was presented to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the local court for interrogation yesterday.

Widening Song Park Road

The Municipal Government Instructs the Land and Public Works Bureaus to Handle Separately

Regarding the case of planning to widen Song Park Road on Xizang Road, the fifth meeting of the first standing committee of the Provisional Municipal Council has re-examined and resolved the matter. Yesterday, the Municipal Government issued Instruction No. 4188 to the Land and Public Works Bureaus to comply. The instruction stated that the Land and Public Works Bureau had submitted a map to the government regarding the planning and widening of Song Park Road on Xizang Road, which had been submitted to the 219th municipal meeting and approved, and then sent to the Provisional Municipal Council for re-examination. The Provisional Municipal Council replied that the case had been resolved by the fifth meeting of the first standing committee of the council. Therefore, the case was submitted to the 226th municipal meeting, and it was decided that (1) the land should be acquired in accordance with the city's road construction levy regulations, and (2) the removal of buildings obstructing the road on both sides should be extended to April 15 of this year. In addition to replying to the letter and issuing separate orders, the case should be recorded and the bureaus should be ordered to comply with the instructions.

Appeal Verdict on the Embezzlement Case of the Manager of the Day and Night Bank

｜Chen Ziquan Sentenced to Six Months in Prison｜

After the Shanghai Day and Night Bank closed, members were dispatched to clean up the premises under the instruction of the Jian Fa Public Jian. After accountants Jia Pan Zhaobang and Wu Zheng found that Chen Ziquan, the manager of the bank, and Chen Yuqing and Chen Xunqing, the accountants, as well as Huang Huizhong, the son of Huang Chu Jiu, had colluded to embezzle large sums of money, they sued the Second Special Court, which declared them innocent. Lawyers Yan Luqing, Dong Chi, Dong Yu, Xu Yannian, Wang Shizong, and Qin Zemin, representing the creditors, refused to accept the verdict, and presented evidence to the court of appeals. After repeated summonses, the court concluded the arguments and waited for the verdict. At 3 p.m. on the 20th, the defendants and lawyers Yan Luqing and others, representing the creditors, arrived in court one after another. President Zhou and judges Guo and Zhu ascended to the criminal court and ruled that Chen Ziquan was guilty of assisting in the embezzlement of business funds and was sentenced to six months in prison. Chen Yuqing, Chen Xunqing, and Huang Huizhong were found innocent. Chen Ziquan was ordered to pay a cash bond of 1,000 yuan during the appeal period. When he was unable to pay the money, the court ordered him to be taken into custody.

Joint Public Notice from the Two Bureaus Restricting Seats in Public Places

The Public Security and Public Works Bureaus of this city, with the Lunar New Year approaching, public gathering places in the city are sure to see an increase in visitors. There are often greedy people who set up seats without authorization, which poses a risk of overloading. The two bureaus previously sent staff to inspect and restrict the number of seats. Now, after a long period of time, people have become complacent, and as a result, a joint public notice was issued yesterday, restricting the number of seats in the City God Temple, Yu Garden, tea houses, book halls, and other public places, depending on the size of the building. The public notice is recorded below: "Notice for joint publication. In accordance with the regulations, the Public Security and Public Works Bureaus have previously sent staff to inspect and restrict the number of seats in public gathering places in the city in order to avoid overcrowding and the occurrence of danger. However, it has recently been reported that while some people have complied with the measures restricting the number of people, others have become complacent over time and have sought to profit by setting up seats without authorization, which is in violation of the general provisions and should be severely rectified to ensure safety. Therefore, the number of seats is specifically limited, as stated above. It is hoped that people will strictly abide by the regulations. Anyone who dares to violate them will be severely punished without leniency. This notice is hereby given. Director Wen Hong'en, Shen Yi."

Neighbor Shouts Fire Alert After Robbery

＝Fire trucks arrive but are not used＝

＝Robbers Flee During the Shouting＝

At about 7 p.m. the night before last, a siren suddenly sounded in Dachang Lane, Ping'an Bridge, Nanmatou, Nanshi. Residents in the neighborhood panicked and shouted "Fire!" In a moment, they rushed out of their houses with their furniture, causing chaos. The first station of the first district heard of the incident and sent patrol officer Liu Songjian to the scene to maintain order. At the same time, the fire brigades of each district also received reports of a fire and rushed to the scene with their pump trucks. However, there was no fire. Under investigation, it was learned that Wang Fengsheng, a 50-year-old resident of Anhui, who opened Wanhao at the Shanghai military camp and served as the chief of the investigation section in the Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Bureau in the two stations, was suddenly visited by four robbers at about 6 p.m. the night before last. All of them spoke in the local dialect. They broke into Wang's house, rushed into the living room, drove the owner and his family to a corner, drew out their pistols, threatened them to remain silent, and had one robber stand guard next to them and one guard the gate. The remaining robbers went straight to the upstairs and searched recklessly. They robbed a small diamond ring, a sapphire ring, and two gold rings, worth more than 100 yuan, and fled with the loot through the back door. A neighbor learned of this and mistakenly thought there was a fire. They blew the whistle wildly and shouted, "Fire!" By the time the robbery was discovered, it had been more than an hour since the robbery. The robbers had already fled far away. The incident was immediately reported to the station chief, who forwarded it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for verification.

Losses of Hundreds of Thousands of Dollars

The Hengxingtai Oil Factory, across from the Gongyi Yarn Factory on the north bank of the Caojiadu River in West Shanghai, caught fire at 6:25 last night. Hundreds of boxes of oil were stored inside, and once they caught fire, it was very difficult to put out. Although the firefighters worked hard to put out the fire, they were unable to do so. It was not until 9:30 that the fire was extinguished. The internal machinery, oil, factory foundation, and buildings were all destroyed in the fire. Wang Jinsheng's Bulging Abdomen

18 Pounds of Opium Found

Gunshots in the Crowd

Li Afu Wounded and Falls to the Ground

Wang Quansheng, a native of Ningbo who traffics in opium, was carrying 18 pounds of opium on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 2:15 PM. While passing by Baifuli near Broadway and Yadong Road, he was accosted by more than ten Japanese ruffians, and they started arguing. Upon hearing the commotion, Huapu Officer No. 1990, Huatanmu Wang Runhe, and Detective Zhang Shoushan from the Hongkou Police Station rushed to the scene. Seeing Wang's bulging abdomen, they immediately arrested him and found the opium on his person. Unexpectedly, someone pulled the Huapu officer's collar from behind, and the rest of the group crowded around and blocked him. In desperation, the Huapu officer drew his gun and fired four shots backward, hitting one person who fell to the ground. The injured person is named Li Afu, a native of Ningbo, 39 years old. The rest of the crowd fled in all directions. Wang was taken to the police station along with the opium, and the head officer ordered him to be detained. Meanwhile, the injured person was taken to the Tongren Hospital and then transferred to the Police Hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, the police station escorted Wang Quansheng to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the facts of the case, adding that Li Afu was injured in the right arm, buttocks, etc., and was unable to appear in court due to being hospitalized, requesting a postponement. The defendant claimed at the police station that he worked on the "Gonghe" transport ship and planned to take the opium to a certain opium den in the French Concession for sale. Li Afu, the injured party, claimed that he did not know the defendant, was a crew member on the "Pinghe" ship docked at Wusongkou, and was passing by the area when he saw the defendant arguing with the ruffians and tried to mediate. The opium was presented to the court for inspection. Subsequently, Huapu Officer No. 1990 submitted a report admitting to firing four shots in self-defense. Lawyer Ge Zhaoji, representing Li Afu, stated that Li Afu had nothing to do with the opium case, was just passing by when he was shot, and that the Huapu officer should not have fired randomly into the crowd. Judge Zhao Linyu briefly questioned the defendant and ordered him to be remanded in custody pending Li Afu's recovery and further questioning.

Hu Xiyuan Discusses the Future of China's Light Bulb Industry

The recent dumping of Japanese light bulbs has attracted widespread attention. Yesterday, Mr. Hu Xiyuan, General Manager of the China Ya'pu'er Electrical Appliance Factory, discussed the current state of China's light bulb industry, stating that domestic light bulb factories began to emerge around 1920, gradually increasing in number. In 1921, a Cantonese businessman established the Guangya Factory, the largest in scale. There was also the Japanese-owned Bolian Factory, which produced a significant number of bulbs. Unexpectedly, due to competition from foreign light bulb merchants, bulb prices plummeted, and the light bulb factories established in Shanghai successively closed down. Those with strong capital struggled to survive and had to cease operations. 1928 was the most prosperous period for small electric bulbs used in Chinese flashlights. At that time, the cost of small electric bulbs was just over two yuan per hundred, and the market price could be sold for more than four yuan. Therefore, small electric bulb factories sprang up everywhere like mushrooms after rain. Until last year, a large number of Japanese small electric bulbs were imported, priced at only 1.20 yuan per hundred, causing more than 95% of China's small electric bulb factories to close down. To perfect and reduce the cost of electric light bulbs, the cooperation of experts in electrical engineering, chemistry, and mechanics is essential. At the same time, substantial capital is needed to support their operations, and highly experienced personnel must manage them. Scientific management and rationalized production are necessary to achieve high-quality production and low costs, leaving room for survival. Currently, a large number of Japanese bulbs are being imported. Although the government can impose dumping taxes, dumping is not unlimited and must comply with dumping laws to be applicable. If China's light bulb industry is to survive, each factory must work hard on its own. If they rely solely on antidumping measures as a protective shield for their business, without researching the principles of production and reducing costs, and if they start light bulb factories with a speculative nature, they may repeat the disastrous failure of 1922, and the future is not optimistic.

Inspection Reports of Two Banks

Central Bank's 149th Report on Issuance Reserve states: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this council is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the Bank's issuance of convertible notes. On January 20, 1933, Supervisor Yu Qiaqing held the 149th inspection at the Bank's Issuance Bureau. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) Total value of convertible notes issued: 43,420,347 silver dollars, including 39,500,533 silver dollar notes and 3,919,814 subsidiary currency notes. Total value of the convertible note reserve: 43,420,347 silver dollars, including 35,491,347 silver taels in cash reserve, stored in the Bank's Issuance Treasury (31,414,952 taels), branch offices in various ports (2,229,647 taels), and deposited with other banks (1,846,748 taels). The security reserve is equivalent to 7,929,000 silver dollars. (B) Total value of customs gold convertible notes issued: 425,000 customs gold units. Total value of the customs gold convertible note reserve: 425,000 customs gold units, including US$170,000 deposited with other banks in this port, at a fixed rate of 0.40, equivalent to 425,000 customs gold units. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's regulations on convertible notes, 60% is cash reserve and 40% is security reserve. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the security reserve is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby issued. January 20, 1933, Central Bank Supervisory Council.

Re-publication of the History of Chinese Journalism: The book "The History of Chinese Journalism," printed by the former United Bookstore, is a monumental work on journalism research by Mr. Huang Tianpeng during his studies in Japan. Book review introductions are representative works of the journalistic field. The entire book is divided into five major chapters: Introduction, Origin, Evolution, Current Situation, and Future of Chinese Journalism, totaling hundreds of thousands of words. Former international student agent Luo supervised and praised it highly, calling it an unprecedented masterpiece. The appendix includes a survey of national newspapers, a news catalog, etc., and the first chapter discusses the origin of news, and the last chapter discusses the future of news, with unique insights and particularly valuable. The chapter describing the current situation is a must-read for those engaged in the news industry and the general public. Therefore, since its publication, it has been popular overseas. The United Bookstore has since ceased operations due to the book's closure. Each book is still sold for 1.50 yuan. Distributor: Modern Bookstore on Sima Road in this port, and various new bookstores in other ports also act as distributors.

Dear Editor: I recently saw in your newspaper, in today's local news section, that Chen Rongcai, a tea server on the Wuchang steamer, escaped with more than 90,000 yuan worth of gold bars brought from Hankou. Reader Consultant

Academics and Schools

| Mr. Jianming's Letter |

I am a student about to graduate from high school, only eighteen years old this year, seemingly a youth capable of great achievements. However, when I graduated from elementary school, my grades were also very good, but due to a momentary lapse in judgment, I mistakenly entered a cramped junior high school, and also became a commuter student, so I wasted three precious years in idle living. Now, thinking back on it in the quiet of the night, I feel nothing but regret! I regret having taken the wrong path, and I hate my own ignorance. But when it came time to graduate, my ranking in the exams was still in the top ten. Is this because everyone else was just muddling through? Later, I tried to apply to high school, but I was rejected the first time. It was only then that I felt my own learning and knowledge were insufficient, but it was too late for regrets, and I could only sigh in vain. Finally, I actually got into a provincial high school, which made me very happy and comforted. So, in the few years of high school, I worked very hard, and I could be considered one of the top students in the whole school. Time flies like an arrow, and now there are only six months left until graduation. So, a difficult hurdle is approaching before me. (That is, the two diverging paths of further education and employment lie before the general high school student.) As far as my aspirations are concerned, I very much want to pursue further education, to gain deeper knowledge and develop a sound personality. Now there are two difficult problems swirling in my mind…

㈠ Will going to university really increase our students' knowledge, learning, and character? Most of the universities these days (private ones) are mostly just diploma mills. As long as you pay the fees in full, you don't even have to attend classes. You can go to the movies or go dancing every day. The situation inside the school is truly chaotic and full of shameful behavior. This not only fails to gain knowledge and learning, but also taints a pure personality, only to add a consumer to society, and in the future, they will not be able to improve the country, but instead push the country closer to the path of destruction! Even national universities are often plagued by turmoil, making such a fuss that it's impossible to concentrate on studying. Perfection is ultimately rare, so going to university is very dangerous. My views are very narrow, and I don't know if this is really the case?

㈡ How to manage the expenses for further education? My family is already struggling to provide my tuition fees, but other expenses will have to be cut back. Moreover, my father is already over fifty years old. He is suffering for his son, and I can't bear it, even though I am the only child. Thinking this way, after graduating from high school, should I look for a job and start life as a warrior in society? (My mother often advises me in this way as well.) I am now worried about my future, wandering at the crossroads of life, and with my views being so immature, it is easy for me to fall. So now I especially ask a learned gentleman to point out a path of light for a lost lamb, so as to avoid his downfall.

Reply: Regarding the two points you asked in your letter, I respectfully reply as follows: ㈠ Regarding the school selection for further education. Diploma-mill universities are indeed slovenly, but aren't national schools also slovenly? If we calmly and quietly criticize them, we can say that they "each have their strengths and weaknesses," but we can also say that they are "not good products," because the advantages of national schools are: (1) More ample funding, (2) Relatively more professors, among whom there are more with specialized knowledge (naturally, this is only relative), (3) More complete reference books and experimental equipment. However, they also have their disadvantages. The faculty and staff of universities are close to the government, and their bureaucratic tendencies are too strong. Even if there are one or two enlightened people, they are in an environment of universal conformity, and there is no possibility of freely developing independent theories. If you want to be a county magistrate or a judge, then you must enter the political science and law department of a national university. If you want to be an engineer, then you must enter the engineering department of a national university. If you want to do research in ordinary social sciences (bourgeois social sciences), then you can also enter the sociology department of a national university. But if you really want to study social sciences based on dialectical materialism, then you don't need to bother asking about it, because they don't sell such goods there. If you go, it will definitely be a waste of effort. As for diploma-mill universities, naturally most of them are trying to cheat people out of money, engaging in empty transactions. However, if you carefully investigate, you may find some fairly good diploma-mill universities. If you come across such a diploma-mill university, then you will see that it has the following characteristics: (1) Some of its professors are full of novel ideas, (2) Its academic atmosphere does not carry much bureaucratic stench, (3) Its teaching materials are relatively free, (4) Students have more opportunities for free discussion. These advantages are not easily obtained in national schools. In the reporter's humble opinion, the future academic atmosphere must rely on good private universities to salvage it. National schools only cultivate some conformist talents, or perhaps a few geniuses may emerge from there, but that is not due to their educational power, but rather to social causes. You believe that those who "cannot improve the country, but instead push the country closer to the path of destruction" must be private university students, namely diploma-mill university students, but that is not necessarily the case! ㈡ Regarding your financial problems for further education. Since your family can "barely provide your tuition fees," then that is not a problem. Even if your family "reduces some other expenses," and your father is only your only son, then naturally he would be willing. If you really feel sorry for your father, then reduce your living expenses even more. Besides the necessary tuition and board fees and necessary book fees, don't take a penny from home. Fortunately, universities are relatively free, and you can still write articles and submit them to newspapers, or do some work for others. Japanese university students sell newspapers in the morning, and American university students wash dishes in restaurants in the evening. They can all earn a few coins to subsidize their expenses, and also take this opportunity to learn more about the life of the poor and get to know the true situation of poor people's lives. Then, on the one hand, you can earn money, and on the other hand, you can also put into practice the maxim of "going to the people." If you really want to live the life of a warrior in society, then you can fight anytime and anywhere, and everywhere is a battlefield. So, muster up your courage. You don't have to look for a job to "start." Our life is struggle. Without "struggle," life has no meaning. What do you think?

A Word to Mr. Wang Yangshan: Your letter has been forwarded to your son. Please provide your address so that we can discuss by correspondence. If publication is possible, it will still be published in this column.

Important News

Zhu Jiahua Cables Zhejiang to Expedite Tuition Fees for Police Cadets Studying in Austria

Provincial Government Has Ordered Finance Department to Remit

Lu Diping, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, recently received a cable from Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Education, stating that a cable had been received from Vienna, Austria, saying that the tuition fees for the police cadets studying in Austria had not arrived for half a year, and they were in extreme hardship. He earnestly requested a prompt remittance of fees for several months to maintain their studies. Since the amount is not large, but it has a significant bearing on the reputation of the country, he specially cabled to inform him, hoping for an immediate remittance. The Provincial Government, considering that the Austrian Embassy and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had previously sent cables regarding this matter, had already instructed the Finance Department to investigate the case. Yesterday, they specifically ordered the Finance Department to investigate the case and allocate funds for immediate remittance.

Jiangsu Education Department Orders County Education Inspectors to Submit Reports

Failure to Submit Reports for Both Semesters of the 21st Year Will Result in a Major Demerit

Failure to Submit Reports for One Semester Will Result in a Reprimand

Since Director Zhou took office at the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department, he has actively reorganized and is very seriously auditing the inspection reports of the county education inspectors and education committee members in each county. The timely submission by each county is strictly enforced. Most counties are able to submit their education reports on time. However, a small number of counties have not yet submitted their inspection reports for the first and second semesters of the 20th year. In addition to separately sending cables to urge them strictly, the members of Jiangning and other counties who have not submitted reports for both semesters will be given a major demerit. For members such as those in Wujiang County who have not submitted the second semester reports, they will be given a lenient reprimand and ordered to submit the required number of reports for review within ten days of receiving the cable. Failure to comply will result in severe punishment. As for the inspection reports for the 21st year, it is said that the order remains the same as before, with the bureau submitting the reports to the department for review within one month after the end of each semester, and no delays will be tolerated.

Anhui Province Replaces Four School Principals

Second, Third, Fifth Girls' High Schools and Seventh Vocational School

(Anhui News) On July 7th, the Anhui Education Department proposed to the Provincial Government to replace the principals of four provincial secondary schools. Luo Mengping of the Second Girls' High School will be assigned to another position, and Ni Shixiong will be appointed to replace her. Ni is a graduate of Zhongda University and is from Hefei. Zhang Bingren of the Second Girls' High School was approved to resign and replaced by Zhai Daxun. Zhai is from Jing County and graduated from the Law and Political Science University. Shu Dejin of the Fifth Girls' High School was approved to be replaced due to incompetence and replaced by Yin Yunhuai. Yin is from Jiangsu and graduated from the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts. He previously served as the principal of the Third Girls' High School. Zhao Jiazhang, the principal of the Seventh Vocational School, will be assigned to another position, and Li Shouqi will be appointed to replace him. Li is from Changzhou and is currently a secretary appointed by the Education Department. It is said that several more schools will be reassigned within days.

Beijing Municipality to Add Ten Primary School Grades First

In order to provide relief to children in the capital who are out of school and to promote universal education, the Beijing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has decided to expand the grades in newly built school buildings. It has now been decided that, starting from February, schools receiving increased grade funding include: Pukou Primary School, adding two grades (originally one grade); Lao Jiangkou Primary School, renamed Xiaguan Primary School after moving to the new school building, adding two grades (originally two grades); Gulou Primary School, adding three grades (originally five grades); and Santiaoxiang Primary School, adding two grades (originally eight grades). This totals ten new grades. Furthermore, based on needs and the availability of school buildings, further additions will be considered. It is reported that in areas such as Gaojing Hutong and Fei Lane, primary schools are being planned for rented buildings, and grade additions are also planned. Municipal schools will close for vacation on the 18th and reopen on February 1st, with classes scheduled to start on Monday, February 6th.

U.S. Department of Labor Issues New Order Prohibiting Foreign Students from Working Part-Time

Chinese Ministry of Education Responds to Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Refuting the Order

After the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, based on a report from the Consulate General in New York, submitted a request to the Ministry of Education regarding the U.S. Department of Labor's promulgation of a new order prohibiting foreign students from working part-time, the Ministry of Education immediately consulted for a reply. Yesterday (the 20th), the Ministry of Education replied, "The Ministry has already formulated a unified policy on studying abroad, strictly dispatching those on government scholarships, and intends to raise the qualifications for private students, so as to ensure that those who go abroad to study are all going for advanced academic research and will no longer seek employment outside of their studies. Although the new order of the U.S. Department of Labor will not have a significant impact on Chinese students studying in the U.S., the cancellation of part-time work, the payment of security deposits, and the restriction on the length of study for foreign students are contrary to the spirit of international cultural cooperation and conflict with equal treaties. Furthermore, students receiving scholarship awards and loan scholarships are purely the result of academic efforts, and such rewards should not be restricted. Therefore, it seems appropriate to state the reasons for the above points to the U.S. government." The details of the U.S. Department of Labor's prohibition of foreign students from working part-time and its impact on Chinese students studying in the U.S. are described as follows:

The U.S. Secretary of Labor announced on September 26th of last year an order to cancel the right of foreign students to work part-time, which has aroused fierce opposition from the U.S. education community. According to the interpretation of the new order, foreign students in the U.S. who are allowed to enter the country under the non-immigrant quota of the immigration law must prove that they have sufficient financial preparation and reliable guarantees to maintain their student life and identity. Regardless of whether foreign students are already in the U.S. or will be allowed to enter the U.S. in the future, if they engage in extracurricular business or domestic service for profit or compensation, the immigration authorities will consider them to have lost their student status, and they may be arrested and deported. Furthermore, after a foreign student is allowed to enter the U.S., there must be a fixed number of years, and when the limit is reached, they must leave the country, regardless of whether their studies have been completed. (Previously, foreign students in the U.S. who were indeed attending school in accordance with the regulations were not subject to any length restrictions.) Furthermore, starting from October 1st, the Department of Labor authorized each open immigration bureau to require foreign students coming to the U.S., if the situation is deemed "suspicious," to pay a security deposit of US$500 before being allowed to enter the country. After the promulgation of the new order, the U.S. education community opposed it fiercely. The Department of Labor's attitude has slightly softened. According to a letter from Harry E. Hall, Director of the General Immigration Bureau of the Department of Labor, to Dr. John H. MacCracken of the Education Association, the degree of restriction in the Department of Labor's regulations prohibiting foreign students from working has been slightly modified. Foreign students who were already allowed to enter the country before August 1932, if they are indeed attending school in accordance with the regulations, are allowed to continue working, but their compensation is limited to room and board and they may not receive wages. They are also allowed to continue working during vacations, but it is still limited to maintaining room and board. Furthermore, foreign students who entered the U.S. in August 1932 are allowed to receive scholarship awards or loan scholarships. According to statistics from the Universal Education Association, there are currently approximately 5,000 foreign students in the U.S., including 1,300 from China, 1,000 from Japan, 500 from Russia, 400 each from the United Kingdom and Germany, 200 each from Italy and India, 150 from France, 125 from Korea, and 100 each from Scotland, Ireland, Panama, and Switzerland, 70 each from Sweden and South Africa, and 20 from Wales. Furthermore, according to statistics from the Immigration Bureau, from June 30, 1929, to July 31, 1922, a total of 4,716 foreign students were allowed to enter the U.S. According to estimates from various parties, the number of foreign students affected by the new regulations is over 1,500.

Since the promulgation of the new order, public opinion has been quite opposed, and the education community has been particularly fierce. University presidents and individuals in the education community have sent letters and telegrams and broadcast speeches on the radio opposing the order. It is reported that the career services departments of Columbia University in New York and Harvard University in Boston are continuing to provide introductions to foreign students and have not strictly followed the new order. Based on this situation, the implementation of this new order prohibiting foreign students from working may not be very smooth. However, in reality, the U.S. is currently experiencing an economic downturn and high unemployment. It is not easy for American students to find part-time work, and the difficulties for foreign students in the U.S. are even more evident. As far as Chinese students studying in the U.S. are concerned, there are more than 1,300 students in public and private universities and specialized schools throughout the U.S. Except for students from Tsinghua University and those dispatched by the Central Party Headquarters who do not have economic problems, most of the students on provincial government scholarships cannot remit their tuition fees on time. As for private students, except for a portion, most have experienced economic difficulties in the past two years due to the decline in the price of silver and have had to seek work outside of their studies to make up for the shortfall. The implementation of the new order will have a significant impact. It is found that Chinese students studying in the U.S. had two different statuses before the new order was promulgated: (1) Students who came to the U.S. before 1924. There are still quite a few of them in the U.S., and most of them have already graduated and have decent jobs to support themselves. The Immigration Bureau has always adopted a laissez-faire attitude towards these students and has not inquired about them. After the promulgation of this new order, it is not clear whether it will affect these students. (2) Students who came to the U.S. after the implementation of the new immigration law in 1924. The restrictions have always been very strict, and this new order is actually targeted at these students. After the promulgation and implementation of this new order, there are also several points that will affect future Chinese students studying in the U.S.: (1) They will not be able to receive scholarship awards and loan scholarships. It is found that quite a few Chinese students studying in the U.S. have previously received assistance from public and private scholarship awards or loan scholarships. After the implementation of the new order, they will not be able to enjoy this right. (2) They must pay a security deposit for entry. The new order authorizes each immigration bureau at the port of entry to require foreign students coming to the U.S., if they are deemed suspicious, to pay a security deposit of US$500 before being allowed to enter the country. Although it does not order all students coming to the U.S. to pay the deposit, the Immigration Bureau usually interprets regulations broadly, and is particularly strict towards Eastern Asians. In the future, Chinese students studying in the U.S., except for government-sponsored students dispatched by the government whom the Immigration Bureau cannot refuse, must prepare sufficient security deposits to prevent difficulties upon entry. (3) Length restrictions. The new order stipulates the number of years that students can stay in the U.S. The student declares this themselves upon entry or it is noted on their passport. However, once it is stipulated, it cannot be extended. Even if the student has not completed their studies when the term expires, they may have to leave the country. (4) No work opportunities. After the new order is promulgated, Chinese students will have no opportunities to work, which is self-explanatory.

Opportunity to study. The internal setup includes basic and clinical departments. The basic department temporarily establishes a Department of Biochemistry, scheduled to open on February 15th. The clinical department is setting up Internal Medicine, Tuberculosis, Dermatology and Venereology, Orthopedics, and Obstetrics and Gynecology departments, scheduled to open on March 1st.

The Vocational Education Society Publishes a Theoretical and Practical Treatise on Vocational Education

Divided into Eighteen Chapters, Totaling 200,000 Words

The Most Complete Specialised Book on Vocational Education

"The Theory and Practice of Vocational Education" is published by the Chinese Vocational Education Society, on the one hand, to commemorate the society's fifteenth anniversary, and on the other hand, to contribute to those in the country who are engaged in research or promote vocational education as a reference. The book is compiled by various experts on each vocational classification. It is divided into eighteen chapters, including Jiang Hengyuan's preface, Chen Xuanshan's theoretical basis of vocational education, Huang Yanpei's concise history of China's vocational education, Zhong Daozan's overview of vocational education in Europe and the United States, Wang Shuncheng's agricultural education, Jiang Hengyuan's rural improvement, Hu Shuhua's industrial education, Zhao Zongyu's commercial education, Yang Lian'e's home economics education and vocational replenishment for women, Pan Wen'an's professional education, Chen Xuanshan's vocational remedial education and vocational courses, Jia Guanren's vocational training, Chen Xuanshan's vocational education teachers, Yang Lian'e's special vocational education and vocational cultivation, Chen Xuanshan's vocational guidance, Huang Yanpei's conclusion and the editor's commendation, etc., totaling more than 200,000 words. It covers almost all aspects of vocational education's theoretical and practical management methods. It is very suitable for educational institutions to adopt as a textbook or to prepare as a reference book. It has now been published, and sample sheets and discount coupons are available. Enclose two cents for postage when requesting by mail. Hardcover is one yuan and six jiao, and paperback is one yuan and three jiao. The distribution points are the society on Hualong Road in this city and the Life Bookstore on Taoerfeisi Road.

Tongji Defeats Jianhua by One Point

In a battle of evenly matched forces, tension was inevitable. Last night's first match between Tongji and Jianhua saw both sides making gains, and it was difficult to tell who would win. Gradually Revealing True Skills

Military Academy Basketball Team Defeats St. John's by a Large Margin

| 48 to 28 Points |

Li Gongyu's Wonderful Baskets Receive Full Court Applause

The Players Are Becoming More Familiar With the Court and Have Improved Greatly Compared to the Previous Night

There Will Be a Fierce Battle Tomorrow Night Against Xiqing Pirates

The Central Military Academy basketball team defeated St. John's by a large margin of 48-28 at the Xiqing basketball hall last night. This was the Military Academy's second match in Shanghai. The team made their debut the night before and lost to Shanghai Industrial School due to unfamiliarity with the court. Last night, they gradually entered a better state and displayed their prowess. Many of their beautiful plays were praised. The Military Academy will battle the Xiqing Pirates tomorrow night.

Entering a Better State

The Military Academy's performance last night was a great improvement over the previous night, restoring their original condition. Their left forward, Li Gongyu, who has the most accurate shots and the nimblest movements, made many wonderful baskets. His accuracy and beauty were indescribable. The two guards were also unyielding. The team's cooperation also improved greatly in the second half. Their passing and movement were very coordinated. From this, it can be known that the last two matches will be even more spectacular. It is a pity that the team lacks a center. Huang Jianding is relatively weak. If they could get a strong center, the team's strength would be increased a hundredfold.

Sailing Smoothly

St. John's was formed by combining two teams, one from a university and one from a middle school. Although the middle school team is good, they lack experience. Li Gongyu and Wang Shixuan each scored two baskets for the Military Academy, taking an early lead of 8-2. St. John's substituted Zhou Xuexian, and indeed, Zhou and Cheng Jingxing also scored three baskets, tying the score at 8-8. However, Gao Lingzhao and Huang Jianding added another seven points, and from then on, the Military Academy sailed smoothly. St. John's trailed by six or seven points, and at 20-12, Cheng Jingxing made two beautiful shots, recovering four points. At the end of the first half, the Military Academy won by 24-16.

Fighting More Bravely

After a ten-minute break, the Military Academy's five players fought more bravely, smashing St. John's defense. They scored basket after basket, adding ten points in a row, making the score 34-17, a difference of twice as much. Li Gongyu made every shot he took, and the Military Academy's momentum grew stronger. St. John's trailed by about twenty points. The final result was 48-28.

Pirates Watching

Last night, members of the Pirates team, such as Smith and Pi Lei, watched the battle from the sidelines, studying the strengths and weaknesses of the Military Academy in order to prepare for their match on Monday night. They all said that their shooting accuracy was astonishing, their center was somewhat weak, and their guards were strong. They constantly discussed how to deal with them, and it is known that their hearts must have been pounding.
