Essays

The Intense Luminosity of a Meteor

— Zhan Lu

In the past, the Netherlands saw a meteor like a ball of fire, illuminating the night as if it were day. As it flew, it sounded like thunder, and it disappeared into the North Sea. Recently, a meteor was also discovered in Wuzhou, Guangxi. Its luminosity was so intense that it was rarely seen, and it had a long, sweeping tail of light, like an enlarged "Nine Dragons Drawing Water" firework. It flew straight to the center of the city, gradually disintegrated, and disappeared! Where did that intense luminosity go in an instant?

"Half black, it still has bones; completely red, it has already turned to ashes." This is a poem by an ancient person describing the exhaustion of charcoal, and it implies that luminosity should not be too intense. If this star only emitted a faint glimmer in the sky, it could permanently maintain its position in the sky. How could it disintegrate and disappear? Its disintegration and disappearance were only because it was going mad. It demonstrated its intense luminosity to the people, stimulating their eyes and preventing them from looking directly at it.

A star with excessive luminosity is a mad star. A country with excessive luminosity is a mad country. Why did Napoleon, the French Emperor of the 19th century, and Wilhelm, the German Emperor of the 20th century, ultimately fail? It was because they wanted to demonstrate their intense luminosity to the people of the world, stimulating the eyes of the people of the world and preventing them from looking directly at them.

The Greatness of the Chinese People

— He Ruo

National shame days number in the dozens, and more are still being created.

Forty thousand square miles of land were lost in one night, along with thirty million people.

Protests and diplomatic notes can resist Japan's sea, land, and air forces.

It is expected that the League of Nations will take the lead, the American navy will be on the right flank, and the Soviet Russian army will be on the left flank to defeat Japan and regain the three northeastern provinces.

Even after a city is reduced to scorched earth, one can still enjoy a cup of wine with the enemy. While the national army is at war with the enemy country, the navy can still maintain strict neutrality.

Chinese soldiers are also politicians, diplomats, lawyers, and X and X. In short, they are "omnipotent."

To the Road of Depravity

— Wu Hezhou

| What Ruined Her? |

A friend, Mr. Bai, had a neighbor in the front building who employed a maid. This maid was very young and was hired as a "young nanny." She was from Changshu and seemed to have arrived in Shanghai not long ago. She dressed very plainly and had a very honest demeanor. She seemed to be diligent in her work, and it was said that her employers trusted her very much.

○ ○ ○

Three months later, this Changshu "young nanny" suddenly resigned from her job.

The reason was unknown.

○ ○ ○

One day, Bai happened to meet this Changshu "young nanny" at the West Gate tram station. Oh! She had changed. Originally a "country bumpkin," she had now transformed into a "modern woman." This was evident from her dress and demeanor. She had a perm, a tight-fitting cheongsam, and the curves that are needed to be called "pretty" by the people of Shanghai.

○ ○ ○

Another day, Bai was at the Tianyun Tea House. This place can be said to be a "gathering place" for female waitresses. Unintentionally, he (Bai) discovered that the Changshu "young nanny" was working there.

Making flirty eyes, acting provocatively, telling jokes, laughing wildly... she let customers have their way. She was now "completely different" from what she used to be.

On the road to depravity.

What ruined her?

Poetic Commentary

— Xu Jie

| A Few Heroic Poems |

"Yue Wumu's Manjianghong": The shame of Jingkang is still unavenged; the subjects' hatred, when will it end? I will drive my chariot, crushing the Helan Mountains! The brave will feast on barbarian flesh when hungry, laugh and drink Xiongnu blood when thirsty, and when I have reclaimed our old lands, I will pay homage at the Imperial Palace!

The rampant brutality of the Rising Sun is no different from the Jurchens. In this vast land, how many Yue Fei's are there? How many Qin Huis? And the heroes like Su, Ma, Ding, and Li have all retreated into Soviet Russia. Who will "feast on barbarian flesh when hungry, drink Xiongnu blood when thirsty?" The Jurchens will eventually be defeated, and the fall of the land can be expected. But who will reclaim our old lands?

"Lu Fangweng's Poem for His Son": When I die, I know that all will be empty, but I grieve that I will not see the Nine Provinces united. When the royal army reconquers the Central Plains, do not forget to tell your father at the family sacrifice!

Fangweng lived in a turbulent time and knew that the Southern Song Dynasty could not recover its lost territories, so he had these poignant words. A kind of patriotism overflows from his words. I believe that everyone will die, but it is better to die on the battlefield than under a window. This is what is meant by "all will be empty." But I grieve that I will not see the Nine Provinces united; now there will surely be a day when the Five Continents are united. The mantis stalks the cicada, and the cicada suffers, but the oriole is behind it. Alas, mantis, how can you be so proud!

"Lu Fangweng's Writing of Grief": In my early years, I did not know the hardships of the world; I gazed north at the Central Plains with the spirit of a mountain. Warships crossed the Guazhou ferry in the evening snow; iron horses crossed the Daguanshan Pass in the autumn wind. I boast in vain of being the Great Wall of the border, but the gray beard in the mirror has already turned white first! The Chu Shi Biao is truly world-famous; who can be compared to him for a thousand years?

Unfortunately, we were born in a turbulent time, with smoke and fire everywhere, and drums shaking the sky. The vast land of Yu has become a stage for the brutal invaders to ravage. The spirit of Wen Tianxiang is not acting, and the historical Tao Lin is dead. The heroic spirit of swallowing the Hu and Jie and weeping ghosts is nowhere to be found. Then where can we find the Chu Shi Biao? In the past, I saw a poetic riddle that said, "○ Girls do not know the hatred of national subjugation," followed by the five characters Shang, Zhao, Han, Wei, and Er. It is a poem by a Tang dynasty poet that "The singing girls do not know the hatred of national subjugation; across the river, they still sing the Backyard Flower." Many people know this. Because I thought that after Korea was subjugated by the brutal Rising Sun, there were more loyal and righteous people than in China, and many of the ordinary subjugated girls became prostitutes. They sang and danced with a clapper and red teeth, not knowing the fall of their motherland. There were many such people. Therefore, Korean girls do not know the hatred of national subjugation! Is it only the singing girls of our country? This poem was written by someone who traveled to Korea, and he was moved by what he saw and felt, so he changed one character and made it an exquisite verse. However, in the eyes of the brutal invaders, it will be changed to the character "zhi." Alas! The Japanese call our country "Zhi," which is based on the two characters "Zhina," but it actually curses us with the meaning of "disorganized and fragmented." Looking at how they call Russia "Lu," thinking that once the sun comes out, the dew will dissipate, their cruel and poisonous hearts can be seen.

Liang Ren Gong's Lost Portrait

— Sculpted by Zhang Chenbo

Hometown

— Hu Tiwei

It has been twenty-two years since the founding of the Republic, and the emotional society still seems to have lingering feelings for the old lunar calendar, which all Chinese people say is killable. This was a major holiday five years ago. At that time, businesses did not have to create clever reasons to hang up "Summer Vacation" signs. They could openly close their doors to drink and enjoy the leisure at amusement parks, admiring the tall structures. Red Leaf, who was six hundred miles away from his hometown, because the company had bestowed a dollar on him to buy wine, and because he had pooled funds with several colleagues, managed to get a table and enjoy a drunken meal. Wine is a matchmaker for romance. After the tea and wine, playing a game of chess was considered a relatively well-behaved activity for a young man. On this day, ten people made up two tables. What about the other two? They were smoking cigarettes and practicing their piety in the gambling hall! Losing five dollars, playing three rounds of cards. Suddenly, the company's errand boy brought a quick letter to Red Leaf. It was sent by his brother from C Village, saying that their father's condition was worsening every day, and telling him to return home if he could get away from his company. Red Leaf read a few sentences, and his heart began to pound. He checked the train schedule in the newspaper and could still catch the 5:00 PM night train. He immediately hired a car and rushed to the station.

The ruthless wheels were grinding the image of his father's illness in Red Leaf's mind. It seemed somewhat ominous. Two months ago, his father had been suffering from asthma and could not sleep peacefully at night. Chinese and Western doctors had tried for a month or two and concluded that there was no cure, and they all advised him to move to a different place for recuperation. So Red Leaf sent his father back to C Village. As soon as they arrived home, his mother was taken aback and secretly told Red Leaf that his father had lost the vigor he used to have. Red Leaf saw this every day, so he didn't notice it. Later, he also discovered that his father's instep would swell high in the evenings. There were two common sayings in C Village: "Men fear wearing boots, women fear wearing hats." His mother eventually cried anxiously, thinking that this disease was coming on strongly. Red Leaf planned to stay home to care for his father and not go out for the time being. But his father refused, saying that those who eat other people's food should put public interests first, and I'm not going to die immediately. This kind of illness can drag on for a year or two, so you can go out tomorrow with peace of mind. Red Leaf didn't dare to disobey, so he asked his brother to write letters every day to report on his father's condition. The next day, Red Leaf got up at six o'clock, ate a few mouthfuls of food, and went to his father's room to say goodbye. He only saw that the bed was empty. His mother said that his father had woken up to use the restroom last night, and as soon as it was dawn, he had gone to the back garden to breathe fresh air. When Red Leaf heard this, it was like a thunderbolt striking his head. The doctor's hope that moving to a different place would be beneficial was again dim. He stepped into the back garden, and his father was sitting on a low bamboo chair under the osmanthus tree, wearing a blue satin jacket. His gaunt cheeks and head of white hair looked at Red Leaf from beside his glasses, without moving at all. Seeing his father's desolate and haggard appearance, Red Leaf felt the most poignant grief in human nature. He stepped forward and lowered his hand.

"Dad, I'm leaving!"

His father didn't say a word, but nodded slightly. Red Leaf kowtowed, and he saw two plump feet in black leather slippers. His heart palpitated, and he couldn't hold back anymore. He got up, and tears were already rolling down his eyes. His father still didn't speak, but opened his eyes wide and watched Red Leaf wipe his eyes with a silk handkerchief. The corners of his eyes seemed to be somewhat damp, because Red Leaf had never seen his father cry from the day he was born until now.

Shanghai Night Talks

— Zhang Ruochun

Youths from a Foreign Land

Midnight, January 10, 1933, was my first time setting foot in the "Black Eyes" midnight dance hall.

The poet W, accompanied by an armed comrade from the XX Committee, came to the Silver Leaf Building and invited me to join them for a night's tour of Avenue Joffre.

"Where should we go?"

After a deliberation between the three of us, we finally decided to explore the Black Eyes.

We entered a dark alley, a Chinese old-style residence with red brick walls. Several wind- and rain-battered pine and cypress trees hung in front of the door. We gently pushed the door open, and a pale-faced woman listlessly raised her head and glanced at us.

We handed our overcoats to an old man in a royal uniform and leisurely walked through a corridor with oddly colored walls, where we were stopped by a fair-skinned Russian youth.

He embraced the armed comrade who was with us, saying something in broken English that was hard to understand, as if he was asking for a dance. A strong smell of "vodka" wafted over, making us want to vomit. There were three of us, and we all had the temperament of comrades, so naturally, we weren't afraid of anyone. We invited him to a small square table inside, and the four of us occupied a seat on each side.

Just as we ordered the waiter to prepare four cups of black coffee, the Russian youth asked to shake our hands. He had realized our goodwill in inviting him, and he showed a very apprehensive and grateful expression, talking at length to express his apologies.

This unknown Russian youth could speak English, French, and a few common Chinese phrases. According to him, he considered China as his second homeland. He had previously served as a low-ranking officer under Zhang Zongchang. When he saw the uniform our comrade was wearing, he couldn't help but recall old memories. That's why he couldn't help but embrace him. He solemnly stated that although he was drunk, he had no malicious intent. He expressed his respect for all young Chinese soldiers. Although his actions just now were a bit reckless, they were also a sign of affection.

At this point, he looked at our comrade in uniform and said, "You have such a beautiful face! With the lines of a Greek. For someone as young as you to be willing to go to the Northeast to kill the enemy, there is infinite hope for China's future!"

After drinking a few sips of coffee, he became even more excited. We had no interest in watching the dance moves of the women in cabaret costumes, nor did we pay attention to the black music. We all listened quietly to the tipsy foreign youth's impassioned monologue...

"Ah! Governor Zhang was a great talent among Chinese military men. It's true, he was a warlord, he didn't understand politics, he didn't believe in doctrines, but he was a man, with the spirit of a husband. When I was an officer under him, he treated us very well, like his own brothers. Even if we were owed pay for two or three months, we were willing to be under his command and would not have any resentment. Because as soon as the Marshal had money, he would always distribute hundreds or tens of dollars to us. He was truly a straightforward and good man!"

"Last year, I saw a photo of Governor Zhang published in a Chinese newspaper. A friend told me that he had been assassinated. I burst into tears on the spot, really, I'm telling you, I cried at that time. If I wasn't tied down, I could leave Shanghai, I would definitely go and avenge the Governor!"

As he said this, his eyes flashed with a fiery red light. We said a few words of comfort to him, and we casually discussed many things about the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident. We talked until midnight. The people in the Black Eyes dance hall gradually increased. We walked out of the dance hall together. The foreign youth reluctantly saw us off for a stretch of the road.

As we were about to part, the poet W asked him, "Why are you drinking so much alone?"

"I've been drunk for over a week. I took ten days of vacation from the foreign firm where I work because I lost my love. She's already dead."

He said this last sentence to us: "If you need me, you can come to the Black Eyes to find me. I have given my life to you."

The Financial Market in the Depths of Winter

｜The Market is Deserted and Trading is Scarce｜

A Landscape of Desolation

A Chorus of Collection Calls

A Brief Summary

Yesterday's gold market was sluggish due to it being Saturday, with only half a day of trading in the morning session. The initial cause was a nearly insignificant drop in London's foreign exchange rate by 0.0625. US banks remained unchanged. The Shanghai Gold Exchange saw only minimal fluctuations in the forward silver price. American cotton rose by four to six pounds. Bank telegrams reporting changes remained static. The opening price was slightly higher and flat, at 798.5 taels. The foreign exchange market opened flat for both British and American currencies. The Ningbo guild initiated transactions, immediately pushing the price up to 799.2 taels. However, internal trading within banks showed a firming trend, with forward US dollar prices for January at 28.125 yuan. As the rate eased by 0.0625, the gold price also fell back to 796.7 taels. HSBC's posted rates for both British and American exchanges remained unchanged. The foreign exchange market remained flat, and the gold market also hovered around the 7-8 tael range. There was a brief surge to 98.3 taels, but ultimately, due to low trading volume, and with Hengxing selling off, it receded to within the 8 tael range. After 10:15 AM, there were very few transactions, with prices fluctuating by only a few cents. Collection calls echoed within the market. Later, as the Ningbo guild continued to seek transactions, Hengxing also came to sell off. These two entities provided slight support to the market. Afterwards, the forward foreign exchange market eased slightly, and prices retreated to 797.2 taels. At the closing bell, no large-scale transactions from major players were observed. Swap spreads were low, having fallen to a discount of one tael offered by short sellers. Trading volume was low, and spot dealers were all offering discounts, as spot deliveries from the North Road had repeatedly arrived in Shanghai in recent days. Long positions had been pushing prices higher in anticipation. With the end of the old year approaching, spot dealers had no choice but to bear the pain and rush to liquidate positions. However, short positions were not eager to buy. This is a record of the market conditions for the half-day.

Rising and Then Falling Back, a Decrease of Two Cents

The morning opening was at 798.5 taels, due to the Ningbo guild buying, an increase of 1.1 taels compared to the previous close. Wanxing successfully bought at around 99 taels. Fuyu also bought, reaching 9.2 taels. Although the foreign exchange market opened at the same price as the previous close, it did not show any tightening. Sanjing and Wahby were both selling January US dollars at 28.125 yuan. Although HSBC was buying, it generally felt easier than at the initial opening of 0.0625. Qingfa and Yong sold at above 8.5 taels, and Wupin also started selling. Wupin opened at 797.5 taels, and the highest it reached was only 8.5 taels. It fell to within 8 taels. Wanxing came again to buy, still at 8 taels. Hengyu then came to sell, but struggled to find a counterparty. Wanxing had also reached its limit and withdrew. Retail investors pressed prices down, and within a moment, it fell to 96.7 taels. Yuanmaoyong came to buy, at around 7.5 taels. There was a slight fluctuation, and when HSBC's posted rates were revealed, and there were no changes for either British or American exchange rates, it became peaceful. Yingfeng and Heng entered the market, adding up to 8.3 taels. Wahby was willing to sell February US dollars at 125. Hengxing then came to sell, and it fluctuated and fell to within 8 taels, to 7.7 taels. At this time, the market was quiet. Dadecheng entered the market slightly, reaching 98.1 taels again. Afterwards, the foreign exchange market was also flat, and trading was low. The gold market became deserted from this point on. After 10:15 AM, the closing scene was already visible. Both buying and selling disappeared. Occasional transactions were sporadic. It dragged on for an hour, and then the Ningbo guild was seen successfully buying small quantities multiple times. However, Hengxing happened to be repeatedly selling at the same time, at around 8 taels. They saw each other rising and falling repeatedly for a long time. The banks were extremely quiet at this time. The market was mainly supported by the small number of transactions of these two firms. Although Wupin was on the selling side, it was because major players in the market were watching, and retail investors had withdrawn. Moreover, the market Wupin was responding to was also similarly weak, and it became even more boring. Only price calls were seen on the market, and there were no transactions. Hengxing had attempted to sell twice at a limit price, but was unsuccessful. Finally, the foreign exchange market seemed to have sellers, with May at 375 doing some trading, showing a slight pullback, to 97.1 taels. By this time, it was already close to the closing bell. Because there was a rate disclosure among the firms, the price was ultimately pressed down heavily, and it closed at 797.2 taels (previous close was 7.4 taels). Wupin continued to see the price pressed down to 96.8 taels. It was found that the lingering remnant of the half-day had lasted for quite a while. The highest price was 795.2 taels, and the lowest was 796.7 taels, a difference of only 2.5 taels. As a result, it fell slightly by 2 cents compared to the previous close.

Disclosure Suppressed by Two Cents

The disclosure price, because HSBC's posted price for US dollars remained unchanged at 27.75 yuan, was 864.86 taels, approximately 67.6 taels lower than the closing price, suppressing it by two cents more than the previous close. The posted price for January and February was the same at 799 taels, for March 797 taels, and for supplementary water 798 taels.

Upon inspection, the situation in the market this week was complex. It coincided with swaps. The Weekend Calculation and Dismantling is Mellow

The Wide Angle Falls and then Rises

Yesterday was Saturday. Banks, as usual, did not do any transactions in the afternoon. News regarding bank collection and payment must be calmer than usual. However, the cent dismantling price in the market was still chaotic. From a general observation, the cent price seemed to have fallen more than in the morning market, but in reality, there was no kind of rising or falling to speak of in the fluctuation scene. Only, in the auxiliary coins, the wide angle suddenly greatly fell in the morning market. The noon market slightly returned, but the result was more than half a cent lower than the day before.

Foreign Cent Suddenly Goes Up and Down, Silver Dismantling Still Doesn't Move

The "foreign cent" price in the market was suddenly six hao, two si and one half smaller than the previous afternoon at 7 qian, 1 fen, 3 li, 3 hao, 7 si, 1/2. The noon market rose 2 si and a half at 7 qian, 1 fen, 3 li, 6 hao, 2 si, 1/2. The result was slightly three hao and seven si and a half smaller than the previous afternoon. The "silver dismantling" price was still the same in both the morning and noon markets, at two fen. The markout was also white. Looking at the trend in silver capital, there seemed to be no hope of a rise within the year.

Wide Angle's Fall and Rise is Particularly Fast, Copper Coins Continue to Increase by Two Thousand

Jiangnan Small Foreign Coins rose suddenly by three li in the morning market, at 6 qian, 2 fen and 7 li. The noon market again fell, calculated to be 2 hao and 1/2 smaller, at 6 qian, 2 fen, 4 li and 7 hao, 1/2. The result was 7 hao and a half better than the previous afternoon. The transaction was 9,500 angles in the morning market and 6,000 angles in the noon market. Guangdong Small Foreign Coins fell greatly for no reason. The morning market dropped by 1 fen and 2 hao and a half at 6 qian, 0 fen and 3 li. The noon market slightly rose 5 li 1/2 at 6 qian, 0 fen, 8 li and 1/2. The result was about 5 li smaller than the previous afternoon. The transaction was 110,000 angles in the morning market and 45,000 angles in the noon market. Copper coins continued to extend by two thousand coins at 378,000 coins. The transaction was more than 40,440 strings of coins.

Banks' Half-Day Business, Silver Collection and Payment are Usually Rare

Yesterday, banks' collection and payment with the opportunity of half-day business seemed more leisurely than usual. Chinese merchants collected and paid bills of 2.45 million. Foreign merchants collected and paid bills of 1.78 million, advanced money of more than 1 million, special collection and payment of more than 2.5 million, guaranteed money transactions of more than 1.1 million, settlement collection and payment of more than 4 million, all kinds of goods, exchange taxes, miscellaneous collections and payments of more than 5.23 million, release from warehouse of 700,000, money shop silver public single collection and payment of more than 28.8 million, markout money collection and payment of more than 3.1 million, all road remittances of more than 800,000, closing payment of more than 2 million, and collected cash of more than 500,000.

Foreign Money Buys Stomach and Forgets Laziness, The Market Shape is Leisurely

Yesterday's foreign money transaction in the market, although the appearance was not cold, was actually purely a counterparty transaction. Exchange drawing of bills was 940,000 in the morning market and 1.155 million in the noon market. Banknotes were 62,000 in the morning market and 50,000 in the noon market. Off-market banknotes were 125,000 in the morning market and 85,000 in the noon market. Check transactions were 95,000 in the morning market and 20,000 in the noon market. Bank transactions were 800,000 mutual market in the morning and 400,000 mutual market in the noon market. Various banks' foreign account dealings and collections and payments were only more than 700,000. Banknote entries and exits were more than 1.2 million. Foreign guaranteed money transactions were more than 900,000. Passenger road source was more than 600,000. Qianzhuang foreign public single collection and payment was more than 9.4 million. Foreign markout money collection and payment was more than 1.5 million. Foreign money borrowing entries and exits was more than 1.2 million. Small Qianzhuang transaction was more than 500,000.

Securities

The Bond Market on the Last Day of the Old Year

Retail Investors Have a Collecting Price Rise of Half a Yuan to More Than a Yuan

Yesterday, the bond market was already the last day of the market before the New Year. Because futures deliveries for January must be handled next Monday, and the market will be temporarily suspended after deliveries, the market was quiet. Upon inspection, the spot situation of various bonds on the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange was only 14,000 yuan in total. Among them, disarmament occupied 10,000 yuan, and the rest was still clear. Futures for January were suspended due to preparations for deliveries, so there was only one kind of market for the February term. It opened at more than 920,000 yuan in the morning. In the afternoon, with the price rising back, the market also flowed slightly and transactions were more than 2.3 million yuan. The total was 3.25 million, in which the Salt Tax of the Unification was about 600,000 yuan. The rest was only between 200,000 and 300,000. As for the trend in various bond prices, the front market was extremely flat due to the demand for supply, so the rise and fall was very small. In the later market, retail investors suddenly collected more vigorously, so prices rose back consistently. The result was more than half a yuan better than the day before. Only the present first nine customs bond rose by one yuan and nine jiao compared to the previous week. The entire sixth term futures also rose by up to one yuan and two jiao, it is said.

The New York Stock Market is Strong and then Exhausted

The Xinfeng Foreign Company reported that the New York stock market on Friday initially opened with a very strong rising wind. Hoover and Roosevelt were meeting, and short positions were panicking, and they were replenishing one after another. However, the rising momentum soon slowed down, and transactions became idle. When the results of the meeting were announced, Wall Street, although acknowledging it as constructive, felt that the market situation did not have an immediate need to rise, so the trend became more and more exhausted. Only the closing price of most stocks was slightly higher than the previous day. The total number of transactions for the entire day was 700,000 shares. Yarn and Cloth

The Yarn and Cloth Market is Nothing More Than Some "Equalizing Transactions"

There are Many Changes in the Holiday······It is Still Good to be Stable and Healthy

Longs and Shorts

There is No Need to Work Hard Today

Let us Wait Until After the Holiday to Compete Again

The yarn market in the morning was showing a decline due to Changji selling off, but trading in the market was quite clear, and there were also many changes in foreign cotton. Furthermore, the period for final accounting has arrived, and all business aspects are returning to their results. Both the long and short sides must wait until next spring to determine the victor. The majority of psychology is watching from a high position, and therefore there are more long positions passing the new year. However, the Japanese army's invasion is still fierce. How will it be? It is necessary to expand and contract according to the situation and customer needs.

Human Standard

At the opening in the morning, because American cotton was tired and flat, short positions were adding to their positions, and the prices of all months fell by 3.4 cents. In the afternoon, general retail investors were hedging, because there will be a week-long holiday starting tomorrow. There is no certainty about the period of market suspension, so there were many who were equalizing transactions. The price of each month rose by 1, 2 and 3 cents. American Cotton Withdrawal

American Cotton Speculation Limited Pending Settlement of Relief Bill

New York, January 20th Dispatch: Regarding the cotton market situation this week, the raw cotton market was mostly stable, due to demand from the industry and other sectors. Investment purchases when prices fell were also part of this demand. Spot trading was quiet, but the price basis remained solid. The extent of cotton acreage in the next season is not yet clear. It is said that if the rural relief bill becomes a reality without clauses restricting cotton acreage, then farmers will inevitably increase cotton planting. According to Washington news, the Senate may need to amend the rural relief bill to allocate funds to wheat, while a separate relief plan will be formulated for cotton farmers. This uncertainty limits speculation in the cotton market, and also depresses forward trade in cotton cloth and raw cotton. The House has passed the agricultural appropriation bill, stipulating that the debt amount shall not exceed 75 million yuan. This bill is now awaiting a vote in the Senate.

Grains

Heavy Stock and Sluggish Sales in Hexia Rice Market

Heke glutinous rice Stagnant... Foreign Rice Prices Rise

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, few boats arrived from Hexia. There are over a hundred rice shops in Hexia. High-quality rice is scarce, and mid-grade rice is predominant. Merchants selectively purchase higher-priced rice, causing the market price to drop by 10-20 cents. Only a small amount of thin rice arrived, and retail sales were active, but prices were weak. Early rice market is sluggish, and Yinyuan rice is also weakening. Dujian rice is scarce, and customer glutinous rice is slightly weak. Yangbu glutinous rice is short and close to the price of thin rice.

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, only about a dozen boats arrived. There is a large accumulation of rice in Pudong. With the Lunar New Year approaching, merchants are eager to sell. Fortunately, stores in urban and rural areas made some purchases, and warehouses continued to handle over a thousand piculs of rice. The market shows weakness. The prices of Suxi, Tongbang, and Qingjiao thin rice have stabilized, with only rice from Changbang and Nangang slightly decreasing. Yinyuan rice is oversupplied, and prices have fallen by varying amounts. Duyang glutinous rice remains expensive due to its scarcity, and Bianyuan rice has no market.

(Heke glutinous rice) Yesterday, the foreign Heke glutinous rice market was completely stagnant. Merchants from Fujian and Guangdong originally had a strong appetite for Heke glutinous rice, but due to the year-end closing, they have all stopped and are waiting for the official opening of the new year before inquiring again. There seemed to be some activity in this street the day before yesterday, but because the Hexia market fell yesterday, the local hoarders have all switched to handling Hexia japonica glutinous rice. Foreign rice prices have risen again overseas. First-grade Saigon rice needs 4.56 taels, and small grains are as high as 4.34 taels. Importers are also hesitant. All parties are mainly focusing on consolidation. The market will not be lively until after the Lunar New Year.

Flour Suddenly Surges in the Last Three Months

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, the prices for each month were stable. Although foreign wheat prices were still slightly fluctuating by 2-4 cents, each mill was watching, mainly because of the year-end closing and no intention to release inventory. In addition, the current month's spot goods are still in short supply, and external sentiment is also rising. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the prices for January, February, and March suddenly rose sharply. The current month's trading has to be suspended, and delivery is required thereafter. There are still transactions among merchants, and mills are finding it difficult to replenish their stock. Bullish speculators are selling tightly. The situation for February and March is very good because Tianjin merchants continue to purchase. The prices for April and beyond are flat because merchants have not moved and mills have also slightly released inventory. As for spot foreign wheat, it is said that Canadian wheat was traded for shipment in January and February at a price of 3.56 taels. The price of Australian wheat has not been finalized. As a result, January rose by 1.5 cents compared to the previous day, February rose by 1.75 cents, March rose by 1.25 cents, April rose by 0.15 cents, May fell by 0.25 cents, and June fell by 1 cent.

The Changjiang Gang Procures Over a Thousand Loads of Year-End Goods Last Year

Hardware transactions are extremely sluggish as the end of the lunar year approaches. However, merchants from the Changjiang Gang, such as Hankou, Zhenjiang, Wuhu, and Luzhou, purchased a significant amount of goods yesterday. They purchased over 5,000 sheets of 7-foot English galvanized iron, 4,000 sheets of 6-foot galvanized iron, over a hundred loads of No. 24 to No. 28 plain galvanized iron, two hundred loads of new iron wire, and transactions were also made in small nails (new and from local factories), galvanized iron tiles, and cement. In total, these merchants purchased goods totaling over 1,300 loads. Although merchants and factories from various regions are closing for the year, this is still a significant amount of business.

According to news from foreign firms yesterday, the market for tinplate is rising steadily, and the current stock is very limited, with the date of stockout not far off. Therefore, informed individuals are searching for spot goods in Hong Kong, the Philippines, and other places to bring to Shanghai.

Free Talk

Diversion (1)

— Ti Zhi

My colleague Lao Zhou is a taciturn person, but sometimes I can get a very intriguing and thought-provoking sarcastic remark or two from him. I am also aloof from the world, but I get along very well with Lao Zhou.

One afternoon, the postman came. At this time, I was waiting for a letter from a friend in the reception room. As a result, I only got two New Year's cards in a pile of letters, and I was disappointed. But unintentionally, I found a registered letter for Lao Zhou, which was sent from XX Middle School in Haimen, Zhejiang. I felt very rare at the time, because I knew that this withdrawn Mr. Zhou rarely had anyone communicating with him. But after I walked out of the reception room with two New Year's cards, this accidentally discovered miracle was temporarily forgotten.

In the evening, I sat at my desk feeling bored. I casually picked up a copy of the Records of the Grand Historian and couldn't read a single word. I don't know why, but I thought of Lao Zhou again, and then I thought of the registered letter sent to him that I found during the day. I thought that the letter must have brought many miracles, so I dragged my shoes to his room, wanting to hear about the news in that rare letter.

From a distance, I saw him sitting there, seeming to be meditating on something. I stood outside his door and saw his eyelids tightly closed and his lips twitching slightly. I didn't want to interrupt his train of thought, so I secretly walked into the room, sat opposite him, and quietly stared at his attitude in a daze.

His tightly closed eyes slowly opened. He didn't seem surprised at all to see me sitting opposite him. He invited me to smoke as usual, so we sat face to face and smoked.

"Lao Zhou! The winter vacation is coming soon, are you still teaching next semester?" I couldn't bear this deathly silence, so I asked him very solemnly.

"I'm not teaching anymore." He said, shaking his head at the same time.

"Do you have another high position? Our teaching life is really not a human life!"

"Where can I talk about having any high position? You think... I have to teach twenty-one hours of classes every week here, and I also have to take care of paperwork and manage the library. Every day, including preparing for classes and organizing extracurricular activities, I have to work more than twelve hours. How can I do it?" (To be continued)

Interpretation of War

— Feng Ju

"War" is originally a very ominous term in human society. However, this term is used by oppressors and exploiters as evil, while it is used by the oppressed and exploited as an extremely sacred and solemn action to protect survival and revive the extinct.

Indeed, for the sake of the peace and happiness of the masses, we should oppose war, but this should only refer to "evil wars." If war is for the sake of resisting oppression and resisting exploitation, then it is a revolutionary war, which is the driving force for advancing the times. For history and for humanity, we should not only not oppose "revolutionary war," but also actively participate in it. Because we believe that only "revolutionary war" is the only driving force to eliminate "evil war," and only "revolutionary war" is the only weapon for the oppressed and exploited to fight for survival and freedom.

Our country has been under the oppression and exploitation of imperialists for more than a hundred years. They have universally caused rural bankruptcy, economic depression, mass unemployment, warlord civil wars, and an unprecedented medieval darkness in politics in our country. In particular, Japanese imperialism is now tightening its grip on the throat of our nation, wanting to kill us in one fell swoop. In this situation, can we still indulge in false dreams of peace? Can we still deceive ourselves with the guise of peace? We believe that in order to achieve "true peace" and to end "evil war," we can only launch a broad "anti-imperialist war" at present! If there are still people singing the high-sounding tune of maintaining peace and opposing war at this time, then they are traitors in our national battle line, lobbyists for robbers, and enemies of the oppressed masses!

Therefore, at present, every oppressed person should recognize the true meaning of "war," and every oppressed person should especially grasp the only weapon of "revolutionary war"!

Morbidity (1)

— Li Yun

Another side of the life of a petty citizen

"Even if we Chinese are inferior to others in everything, this cuisine item is not bad, right! In winter, I say, Chinese food is more suitable than Western food." After a moment of silence in the conversation, Lei looked at the steaming dishes laid out in front of him and began to speak to his friends Fang and Tong again. At the same time, he filled his glass with the remaining wine in the pot... then, he ordered loudly to the waiter who was serving a dish... "Heat the wine!" "Chinese food is really not bad! I also love to eat it." Fang went on to say... "The old scholars say... the Chinese are too worshipful of Europe and America, especially the youth, and everything is better in other people's homes. In fact, their words are too arbitrary. We love Chinese food, isn't it good to say that we are lovers of national essence?" He said, laughing.

"Shameless! According to what you say, you can simply portray yourself as a loyal and patriotic warrior!" Tong had an expression that was half solemn and half comical. Suddenly his voice became increasingly indignant... "Hey, have you guys been paying attention to national affairs lately? China should stand up on its own! China should fight bravely! ...... Okay, the wine is here, give it to me!" At this time, the waiter was serving the wine, and he took the wine pot and poured it into his glass.

The sound of a erhu came from another room. Then there was a low and vague female voice singing. Lei and Fang were obviously listening attentively. Tong gave a cold snort at them.

"Listen to his mosquito-like cries! Come, let's drink, cheers to this glass, to bless the future of China, to wish the brave warriors victory!" Tong said, raising his glass and drinking it down in one gulp.

"Alas, why don't you join the army!" Lei said coldly.

"Me! Lao Tong? It's not that I don't have hot blood! It's not that I don't have courage! But the environment is really bad, damn it, the environment is too bad to allow me to join the army. But I want to fight the environment! I want to join the army! Go, go! Go to the Northeast!" Tong said, slamming his fist on the table, then picking up his chopsticks, picking up a piece of food, putting it in his mouth, and chewing vigorously.

Lei looked at Tong's increasingly red face and muttered to himself... "Useless! He can't stand a few cups of wine, his face is already flushed, and he still brags and goes on a drunken rampage!"

"What?" Tong's eyes suddenly bulged out, and he asked angrily. At the same time, unconsciously, he rolled up his sleeves.

"Don't make trouble! Speaking of joining the army, I have some news to tell you." Fang's words interrupted, "Do you know? Lao Jiang is going north to join the army. Do you think this is possible?" (To be continued)

The Liberation of Soviet Women

— Xu

If you are a woman living in the Soviet Union, you have the same rights as men! Whether you want to or not.

You have to work like men, support yourself, and dedicate yourself to the construction of a new society. There, the sexes are absolutely equal. If you work hard, you can participate in any kind of occupation and do any kind of work. Even if you do the heaviest and most uncomfortable labor of men, no one will laugh at you because you are a woman.

You can be a mason, carpenter, street cleaner, cadre of a collective farm, you can also be a raw material manager for a steel-smelting furnace, or a heavy machinery operator, or a butcher, or the minister of the most important electricity department of the government.

The Dnieper Dam, which has now been completed, was built jointly by many women's labor. They are also one of the major driving forces for "completing the Five-Year Plan in four years."

There are two female commanders in the Russian Red Army.

Two-thirds of the students in all Russian medical schools are women.

There are many female workers who also handle legal affairs. As for female architects, they can be seen working alongside male architects in the planning of all new buildings.

There are female drivers in the engine room of locomotives. Female workers are often seen arranging tracks on railways.

The magnificent "Park of Culture and Rest" in Moscow is managed by a young and slender Russian woman.

Krupskaya, that is, Lenin's wife, is tirelessly working to eliminate illiteracy, and she wants to clear it up within a limited time. Thanks to her continuous efforts, the civil education of Russia was completed under this slogan: "By 1933, everyone in Russia must be able to write and read!"

In the Soviet Union, every woman values ​​her personal worth. Being the wife of a Communist Party leader does not make her particularly glorious.

Newspaper reporters did not visit Mrs. Stalin in Russia as they did Mrs. Hoover Coolidge in the United States. (Mrs. Stalin studied chemical engineering and was preparing to go to an artificial silk factory.)

There are really no weak women in Soviet Russia. In the cement buildings near the cooperative farms, they are often entirely female workers. They build walls, they lay floors, open windows, and install lead pipes.

Many new cement roads were made by women. Female bricklayers can be seen on the fourth or fifth floor of new buildings.

This equality naturally extends to all aspects. Soviet men have learned to help them with housework and take their children to the park. Men also have to buy groceries.

Long novel

The Crossroads of the Times and Love (Manuscript Continued)

— Zhang Ziping

However, if such derailed feelings deepen day by day, how will they be dealt with in the future? This is sin! This is Mo Zai's sin! I am a promising youth. I am the future owner of the Republic of China. I must be determined to be a model youth! I must maintain a pure personality!

But his chest was still pounding. His psychology at this moment was like a thief, having set his sights on an object and preparing to seize it.

"Put his arms around her and ask for a kiss..."

He knew it would be easier than picking up something. But he thought, why are my emotions so agitated that I dare not act immediately? He felt a chill run down his spine. He looked at the driver in front. The driver was enthusiastically turning the handle, and had no time to pay attention to the two of them sitting behind him. He looked again at whether anyone on both sides of the car was paying attention to him and her in the car.

"How stupid! Who would look at us? The people coming and going on the road all have their own vehicles. Even if they see us kissing in the car, who would be nosy enough to interfere? Besides, they don't know who we are. The car is also driving so fast that people outside must not be able to see clearly. Kiss her, kiss her!"

He seemed to have made up his mind. But the more he made up his mind, the more his body moved, and the less courage he had to express it. From her body, another subtle fragrance emanated.

The car stopped at the entrance of the park.

"We're here."

Hearing the driver say this, Haiquan woke up from his dream. As if he had lost an important item, he regretted not launching a counterattack against Mrs. Hezi in the car just now. He jumped out first, intending to go and help her out of the car. Mrs. Hezi grabbed his palm tightly.

He gave the driver two dimes for drinks.

"A little more."

The driver still asked him for it.

"I don't have it..."

Mrs. Hezi took out two dimes again and gave them to the driver.

Amateur Ramblings

The People's Sentiment of "Having the Heart to Serve the Country but Lacking the Power to Save It"

— Pu

A few days ago, a reporter in Beijing met a friend who had just come from Beiping. We hurriedly asked him to tell us about the anti-Japanese situation in the Pingjin authorities and the performance of the people's sentiment. This friend immediately looked at us with a mournful face and said the following:

"I knew on the road that when I met you, you would ask me these two questions, because these are also the two questions that I often think about and pay the most attention to. But the more attention I pay, the more disappointing it becomes! Speaking of the local official who is defending the territory, since Yuguan and Jiukou successively fell, sending troops and deploying generals, although there is an expression of determination to resist, they still focus on defense. It seems that there is no preparation for counterattacking the lost territory. If one place is attacked like this, they will resist in that place, and if they can't defend it, they will retreat. They will telegraph the whole country to announce the reason for the failure to defend, and swear that they are determined to resist the enemy, but the result is still inaction, without making preparations to counterattack the lost territory. It can't help but make us think that this is only the wonderful use of the two words "resistance" of retreat and defense. As for what the people have shown, apart from the rich moving, schools closing and students scattering, and the common people sitting in worry, worrying that they will have nothing to eat in the future, there is still a peaceful atmosphere, with very little anti-Japanese organization or other激昂displays. The students of Tsinghua University have two sentences in their presentation to the school authorities requesting early leave and exemption from the final exam: "Having the heart to serve the country but lacking the power to save it"! From these two sentences, we can observe and understand the location of the people's will in Pingjin and the reason for the lack of expression!"

After listening to this friend's words, what is a little bit alarming and most worthy of attention is not those two helpless, extremely demoralizing words "having the heart to serve the country but lacking the power to save it", which can represent the psychology of the majority of the people of the country! We are not surprised by the inability of the North China authorities to turn defense into offense and actively resist. We saw on the afternoon of the 20th (see this newspaper's Beiping special telegram) that Zhang Xueliang said in his speech to all sectors of society at Prince Shuncheng's mansion that "to fight foreign wars, the whole country must be mobilized to achieve results." Standing from the standpoint of the people, we deeply feel that after the Japanese army occupied Yuguan, on the one hand, the central government declared that it was preparing to resist with all its strength in North China, and on the other hand, it still maintained a friendly attitude in various places along the Yangtze River. This unprecedented farcical diplomatic policy in the international community is inherently incomprehensible, so that Mr. Zhang, who originally had no spirit of resistance, did not have the courage to fight a solitary battle, which is also a fact that our common people can understand. As for some people hoping that Zhang Xueliang would disregard everything and imitate the spirit of the 19th Route Army in Shanghai to resist the Japanese, that is another fundamentally wrong and wishful thinking of the Chinese people, failing to recognize Zhang Xueliang's extravagance. But we need to solemnly raise the issue of the performance of the people's sentiment for discussion.

We deeply feel that there are two reasons why the people's sentiment in Pingjin is so depressed this time: first, because in the past year, the North China authorities have not only failed to protect and promote the people's anti-Japanese movement, but have implemented various oppressive measures to avoid giving the Japanese an excuse to cause trouble, so that the majority of inherently cowardly people have sunk into a life of decadence and compromise, thus developing the so-called "having the heart to serve the country but lacking the power to save it" result; second, because the people's organizations are unsound, so although there is people's sentiment but no people's power, it is easier to become decadent and depressed when encountering oppression. Moreover, cowardice and compromise, and the lack of a spirit of resistance, are also a common disease that the Chinese people have developed under the autocratic system for thousands of years. Therefore, to save the current disaster, we should not only pay attention to stimulating the people, but also pay attention to cultivating the people's power. The way to cultivate the people's power is to give the people organized training. With sound people's organizations, there will be great people's power. We believe that everyone with blood and energy feels heartbroken and feels the suffering of "having the heart to serve the country but lacking the power to save it" in the current situation where foreign troubles are so urgent and the whole country is still so lifeless. Therefore, although the reporter does not dare to compliment the Tsinghua students for requesting early leave and stopping the final exam, he expresses considerable sympathy for these two sentences of "having the heart to serve the country but lacking the power to save it", and really can't bear to blame them. Because these are really two honest words, which are much better than the government authorities who superficially sing the high tune of resistance but are actually neither fighting nor making peace and never counterattacking.

However, China is the hometown of the majority of us, and we cannot put the responsibility for this country's demise on one or two people in the government just because we have the heart but lack the power. We should realize that the fundamental reason why the country has reached this point of endless internal strife and external troubles is because we, as citizens, have abandoned our responsibilities, and our people have no organization. Therefore, we have no power to resist strong enemies from outside and eliminate national traitors from within. This is the problem that we should wake up in time and strive to remedy.

Problem Discussion

Three Different Characters

— Xu Nangong

Shop Assistants, Shop Owners and Customers

The Problem of Shop Assistants Being Slow with Customers

This journal has continuously discussed the problem of "shop assistants neglecting customers" a lot, but all of them have focused on the shop assistants' side and ignored the customers' side. Although I am not a shop assistant, I think both sides should be mentioned in the same breath.

The reason why shop assistants neglect customers has been explained very clearly and thoroughly by You Pingxiang, Ding Jingyu, and others in previous issues. In a nutshell, it is because shop assistants have shallow knowledge, despise the poor and worship the rich, and are infected with bad habits. In fact, from their own point of view, they do have a lot of pain. For example, the shop owner's low treatment, long working hours, bad environment, and insecure life are all enough to make them lose interest, feel bored, and feel depressed in their work. Under this kind of state, it is indeed very difficult to increase their work efficiency.

Of course, shop assistants often neglect customers, but sometimes this is also self-inflicted by the customers. Often, some customers do not think or consider what kind of goods they want to buy before entering the store. After entering, they look around aimlessly, or even pick and choose repeatedly without any opinion. Or, after the goods are selected, they are wrapped up and paid for, but they insist on lowering the price and reducing the money, so that the transaction fails and they speak rudely. Therefore, it is also a common thing to cause the shop assistant's psychology of being slow to customers due to various reasons.

Based on the above situation, my conclusion is that to change the attitude of shop assistants being slow to customers, the shop owner must ensure that the goods are genuine, the price is fair, improve the treatment of shop assistants, make them feel at ease to serve, and give them a reasonable amount of time to read books and newspapers so as to improve their knowledge and enhance their morals. Customers must maintain a sincere attitude, be humble and restrained, and do not simply regard themselves as customers and despise everything. Shop assistants should also be calm and peaceful, not perfunctory or noisy, adhere to the spirit of serving the society, and do not add their personal joy and anger to customers. All of the above are also a kind of morality that should be in the commercial field!

Life in the Business and Industry Sector

A Frightening Account of a Newspaper Vendor's Life

— Yinghui

During the Shanghai Battle, I secretly sold newspapers around Yangshupu for five days. Business was really good. The old Shen Bao sold for one dime apiece, and the Shih Pao for 150 cash. I made enough for food, with a little left over. Although I was exhausted and frightened every day, I had to rely on luck and do my best to make a living.

These newspapers were secretly obtained from Wangping Street. Each time I went out to sell, I carried no more than five copies, as too many wouldn't fit under my clothes. If the Japanese soldiers saw them, I'd be finished. Japanese soldiers with rifles were often seen at street corners, but after five days, I became used to the work, and the fear disappeared. Sometimes I even deliberately walked past Japanese soldiers, pretending nothing was amiss.

After selling five copies, I would return home to get another five, repeating this process until all were sold. Little Jinzi and I initially sold about thirty copies a day, later increasing to fifty. The more people who read, the more money we made, but the more dangerous it became. We often heard people saying things like:

"A newspaper vendor in Badaotou was beaten to death by Japanese soldiers."

"Four newspaper sellers were arrested and taken to the Japanese military barracks."

"The Japanese shoot anyone they see selling Chinese newspapers!"

At first, we were afraid, but after getting used to it, we paid no attention to such talk and continued to secretly deliver and sell newspapers from house to house.

"Hey," someone would quietly call out as I delivered newspapers into an alleyway. I knew there was business. Then the person would ask in a low voice, "Do you still have newspapers? What's happening on the front lines?"

I didn't have time to say much. While replying "Yes," I would say, "The Japanese soldiers suffered a great defeat," hand over a newspaper, collect the money, and leave. There were few patrolmen on the streets at this time, but when we did see them, they were always helpful, unlike their usual harsh treatment of vendors. I think this was perhaps because they had seen the brutal face of imperialism during the Shanghai Battle.

I never imagined that I could sell over two hundred newspapers in five days. If I hadn't been so afraid of death, business would have been even better, but I feared not knowing how, where, or when I would die. This was a real problem.

I felt indignant. Why should Chinese people be bullied by foreigners? Chinese territory was taken over by foreigners and called concessions. The Japanese came to China to beat Chinese people.

(Important text continues on page 2)

Page 20

What kind of situation was this? Besides, the Yangshupu area wasn't even Japanese territory. Why did they send troops to stand guard and suppress the Chinese people? If it weren't for this, selling newspapers would be much easier.

"Down with imperialism! We must overthrow imperialism!" I was filled with such resentment and determination by the stimulation and suffering from various sources. So, when I read in the newspaper that some people had joined the volunteer army and were fighting the Japanese soldiers in Zhabei, I thought about becoming a warrior myself, killing the enemy, fighting for the liberation of weak nations, and waging a war against imperialism for the toiling masses. What a great thing that would be! Wasn't it much better than secretly selling newspapers in Yangshupu? But in the end, I didn't go. My reasoning was... Waging war against imperialism and fighting for the survival of weak nations wasn't just about fighting on the front lines. I could sell a few more newspapers in the rear, so that my compatriots could see the newspapers under severe surveillance, learn about the war situation, and be inspired to resist Japan... Wasn't this also an important task? I certainly needed to continue selling newspapers! Even if I were to be sacrificed for selling newspapers in the future, it would be worth it.

One day, just after noon, I hid five newspapers in my waistband, eating a pancake as I walked. Following my daily delivery route, I first went to Ruyi Lane, then to Hongyuan Lane. As I walked out of the entrance of Hongyuan Lane, just as I was about to deliver the last copy to a tobacco and paper shop next to the alley entrance, I heard a rough shout behind me... "Stop!"

At first, I didn't pay attention, but then I heard the sound of a gun cocking. I turned around and realized what was happening. Three Japanese soldiers were standing on Huade Road behind me, aiming their guns and shouting at me. This time I really panicked. What should I do? If I was caught by these three dogs, things would not end well. I couldn't think anymore. The three Japanese soldiers were walking towards me. Ignoring everything, determined to survive this time, I bent down and dashed to the side of the road, where there happened to be a small vegetable market with some people coming and going. I dove into the crowd, ran into a tofu shop across the street, and escaped through the back door. Then I heard two shots. They were naturally shooting at me, but I finally escaped to another road.

I didn't know where I lost a newspaper. Perhaps the three Japanese soldiers picked it up, but what did that matter? Escaping with my life was better than anything. Afterwards, I turned corners and detoured a lot, finally returning to my three-story attic home.

My heart was pounding very hard, and I threw everything I had thought about before out of my mind. Now, the only thing dominating me was "fear." Really, I was afraid. I was afraid that the Japanese soldiers would chase me to this three-story attic, that I would be caught, that I would be shot! How dangerous my situation was! ... I saw the Shih Pao on the floor, and the big red characters on the newspaper turned into a pile of bright red blood, and the black characters on the newspaper jumped up. The broken things in the house also flashed with it! In the end, even the small attic seemed to spin...

Suddenly, the door opened. I opened my eyes wide and saw it was Little Jinzi. "Why aren't you selling? What are you doing hiding in the room?" he asked me. All of a sudden, my mind cleared up a bit, but what did I answer him? I couldn't say.

"What's wrong? Are you dumb?"

This time I completely returned to normal, and all the changes were gone. I told him quietly about what I had encountered, and after I finished speaking, I asked him if he saw any Japanese soldiers walking in front of the door. I was still filled with fear.

"Was it at the corner of the vegetable market?" he asked me. "You were so scared by such a thing, your face looks like white paper! Let me tell you, I was on the south side of the vegetable market when the shooting happened, but I didn't run. I stood there and watched for a long time. Later, the Japanese soldiers found a Shih Pao, and started searching people. It turns out that was the Shih Pao you lost. I'll fine you a pancake." He smiled as he said this.

Commentary

A Plea to Society on Behalf of Vocational Youths

— Aiying

The first lesson vocational youths learn in their service is that their knowledge is shallow and insufficient for application. Nine out of ten want to use their spare time to supplement their knowledge. The attitude of general employers towards this problem can be divided into three types: The first type believes that shop assistants can only be used and not enlightened. Once they are enlightened, it will be a disaster. Therefore, they strongly oppose their studies. Sometimes, if young shop assistants voluntarily attend vocational supplementary schools, it is considered a great act of disobedience once discovered, and they are immediately warned that they will be dismissed if they continue their studies. For the sake of food and clothing, young shop assistants have to submit. The second type believes that shop assistants' studies are their own business, and they are allowed to attend school as long as it does not interfere with their service. The third type believes that although shop assistants' studies are their own business, their service efficiency will naturally improve after their knowledge increases, which is not unrelated to the store, so they generously provide tuition fees. In Shanghai, the first type is still the majority, the second type only exists in modern stores, and not all of them, and the third type only exists in some cultural and financial institutions, which are truly rare. Therefore, there are countless vocational youths who want to study but cannot. The cry of knowledge famine pervades the city. Driven by conscience, I have to make a plea to society on their behalf.

First, I advise employers not to prevent young shop assistants from seeking education, burying their future and hindering the development of your store. Because we are now in an era of commercial warfare, shop assistants with shallow knowledge and low service efficiency will never win. It is best for everyone to send your young shop assistants to school like cultural and financial institutions.

Second, I advise those in society who are concerned about saving the country to use a large part of their energy and strength to promote and support vocational supplementary education, so that a group of young shop assistants who have already awakened can receive good and adequate education and become a vital force in your work of saving the country.

Third, I advise the society to unanimously urge the government to allocate a sum of money to promote vocational supplementary education, and at the same time, include primary vocational supplementary education in compulsory education, forcing employers to send their young shop assistants to school.

Fourth, I advise those who run education to run fewer empty universities and middle schools, and everyone should actively contact the vocational sector to run the most effective vocational supplementary education.

Ah, everyone, prick up your ears and listen to the tragic cries of knowledge famine from vocational youths, and reach out to rescue them!

Self-Employment Introduction

Land Surveyor

— Liang Daohong

"Hey, long time no see. Where are you currently working?" Zhou asked me when he met me on ×× Road.

"Land surveyor in the Chinese and concession areas," I replied.

"Land surveyor? What's that?" Zhou asked in surprise.

"The term 'land surveyor' wasn't newly created by me. It's the only way for unemployed comrades to avoid debt. I've been unemployed for almost a year. My family's clothing, food, and housing have become a problem. Sitting at home, I'm very worried, so it's better to come out and survey land," I explained.

"Surveying land is not a long-term solution. Why don't you think of a way?"

"I don't have great physical strength. Although I have asked relatives and friends for help several times, they are evasive. The recruitment columns in the newspapers are unreliable. What other options are there?"

"Oh! Didn't you know? There is an old lady named Shen Bao, who is over sixty years old, who has opened a matchmaking agency. I heard it's very successful. Why don't you try it?"

"Is that so? I'll go try it right away. Goodbye! Goodbye!"

"Goodbye! Goodbye!"

That afternoon, a man about twenty years old came to that matchmaking agency. According to himself, he was a Cantonese who could speak Shanghainese, was proficient in English, modern bookkeeping, English typing, and commercial arithmetic, and had some knowledge of abacus. He used to work in ×× Foreign Firm, but his job was suspended due to the Shanghai Battle. If any company or foreign firm is willing to employ him in any position, he is welcome. Monthly salary of about thirty yuan. Correspondence address... Please forward to this publication.

Shop Employee Correspondence

The Reality of Shop Owners Exploiting Shop Employees

Editor: In this era of expensive prices and rising living standards, we ordinary shop employees, although we work more than fourteen hours a day, how much compensation can we get? How can we cope with the seven necessities of life? So, year after year, no matter how thrifty we are, no one can avoid some deficits. Fortunately, according to the rules of old-fashioned shops, at the end of the year, there are always some public records, bonuses, etc., which allows us to get through year after year.

Since the "January 28th" incident last year, the foreign goods shop where I work, of course, could not be an exception. The shop owner took the opportunity to declare the cancellation of the public records, bonuses, and other benefits of the shop employees. At first, the partners, considering the store's losses, did not express any resistance, out of the friendship of sharing the same boat. Now that the final settlement period is approaching, although all the accounts cannot be settled yet, a rough idea can already be seen. This year's business in our shop not only will not lose money, but there will also be some surplus. We ordinary shop employees then asked the shop owner to restore the original various benefits, but the shop owner completely ignored us. Isn't this clearly exploiting us?

Editor! How should this matter be dealt with? Please give us instructions as soon as possible. (The following is omitted.) Pan Shaoan

Editor's note: Public records are designated by the shop owner for the sake of caring for the shop employees. They are designated as a certain non-major income of the store that belongs to all partners. Regardless of the overall profit or loss of the store, this type of designated income must be distributed to all partners every year. Its nature is entirely a gift from the shop owner, so in stores that do not have public records according to the past, shop employees cannot make requests. The reason is because the law stipulates that "gift" is a kind of "laissez-faire behavior." However, in stores that have always had this rule, the shop owner cannot unilaterally announce the cancellation, because in fact, for this type of public record income, the salaries of the partners have already been reduced accordingly, and habit also has a huge force in civil law.

Furthermore, the nature of bonuses is to extract a certain percentage from the operating surplus to distribute to the partners as a reward for a year of hard work. Usually, it is clearly stipulated in the agreement. Therefore, if the store loses money, then that's that, but if there is a surplus, this bonus is absolutely not allowed to be deprived.

Based on the above judgments, then Mr. Pan's colleagues should argue on the basis of reason and not give up. However, we know that this year's money supply in Shanghai is extremely tight, and some stores, although profitable on the books, are actually very tight. I hope that Mr. Pan and others will investigate further to see if this is the case. If so, then in addition to arguing on the basis of reason, they may as well make concessions by postponing the payment. Mr. Pan and others who can be considerate of "sharing the same boat" will also think so.
